All Sides Denounce the Fujian Rebellion 14

(Anqing) All sectors held a grand meeting to welcome Commander-in-Chief Liu at the public sports field at 9:00 AM on the 3rd. Wu Zunming, Chairman of the Provincial Party Rectification Committee, reported on the purpose of the meeting, followed by a response from Liu Zhenhua. At around 10:00 AM, a grand meeting to denounce the Fujian rebellion was held, chaired by Zhang Xinnan, Chairman of the Provincial Party Rectification Committee. Five proposals were then passed, and the meeting adjourned. (3rd Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Fujianese residing in Beijing held a joint emergency meeting of all sectors of the Fujian community residing in Beijing on the afternoon of the 3rd. Chairman Chen Yanglian reported on the purpose of the meeting, followed by the adoption of proposals: 1. Request the Central Government in the name of the Fujian Fellow Association in Beijing to issue a clear order to suppress Chen and Li. 2. Request the assembly to petition the central authorities to organize armed hometown rescue groups to participate in the suppression. 3. Request the assembly to organize a permanent organization, the Party Protection and Hometown Rescue Executive Committee. 4. Elect Chen Meian and 10 others as representatives of the assembly. 5. Pass the assembly declaration and the letter to compatriots at home and abroad. After the meeting, the entire assembly went to the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government to petition, but because it was a Sunday, no one received them, and they did not get what they wanted. They changed to continue the petition on the morning of the 4th. (3rd Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Sui Province Party Headquarters telegraphed the Central Government, requesting the suppression of Chen and Li. The original text stated: "Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, and others have betrayed the Party and the country, are pro-Japanese and allied with the Communists, have seized Fujian Province, changed the era name, and established a regime. Their madness knows no bounds, and their crimes are heinous. Various parties have telegraphed to advise them, but they are stubbornly unrepentant. Such people are fond of chaos by nature, are stubborn and unyielding, and should be severely suppressed to quell the riots. We respectfully request your council to inform the National Government to immediately send troops and launch a large-scale attack in order to maintain the Party's foundation and protect the country's lifeline. We telegraphically request this in pain. We beg for your consideration. The Kuomintang of China, Sui Province Party Headquarters, bowing." (3rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Changsha) The Provincial Party Headquarters telegraphed urging Central Committee members from various places to go to Beijing to jointly overcome the national crisis. All sectors have scheduled a propaganda rally against the Fujian [rebellion] to be held early on the 5th at the Zhongshan Hall. (3rd Dispatch)

(Nanchang) All sectors in Jiangxi held a meeting of citizen representatives to denounce the rebellion at the Desheng Stage at 1:00 PM on the 2nd, with over 1,800 people attending. Representatives from various groups gave speeches about the Fujian rebellion, which were deeply felt and impassioned, and five proposals were resolved. (1) Telegraph to the Central Government requesting the suppression of the rebel Chen Mingshu and others. (2) Circulate a telegram nationwide denouncing the rebels. (3) Telegraph urging Central Committee members from various places to quickly go to Beijing to jointly overcome the national crisis. (4) Telegraph requesting Chairman Chiang to suppress the rebels and intensify the suppression of bandits. (5) Telegraph congratulating Chairman Chiang and the officers and soldiers suppressing the bandits. The meeting adjourned at 3:00 PM, and various groups departed in teams to carry out propaganda. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Huang and Zhao Go to Taiyuan to Meet Yan; Departed from Suiyuan Yesterday Morning; Fu Zuoyi Accompanied 15

(Beiping) Huang Shaoxiong and Zhao Pilian went to Taiyuan on the 3rd to meet with Yan for important matters. The funds for Huang and others to go to Mongolia were originally set at 30,000 yuan, but later, due to gifts to various Mongolian princes, a total of 50,000 yuan was spent. Huang has telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, requesting the Central Bank to advance the funds first as formal expenses. (3rd Dispatch)

(Guihua) The telegram reports that Huang and Zhao reportedly departed from Suiyuan on the morning of the 3rd, together to Datong, then transferred to Taiyuan to meet with Yan. All sectors gave them a grand send-off. Huang plans to stay in Taiyuan for a short time. After meeting with Yan to discuss Mongolian affairs and other issues, he will take the Pinghan Railway to Jiangxi to meet with Chiang and report. At that time, he may go to Beiping to meet with He and discuss everything. (4th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Wu Heling discussed the Japanese setting up an autonomous region in Duolun, saying that after the loss of the three northeastern provinces and Rehe, Japan has always coveted western Mongolia and has constantly fabricated various rumors to confuse the Mongolian people. As for the establishment of an autonomous region, he has only seen it reported in the newspapers. When he left Mongolia, he had not heard of it. However, in Duolun, several months ago, Japan established the Chahar East Administrative Commissioner's Office, appointing Li Shouxin as the commissioner, in charge of everything, and brought an army of about 10,000 people. (3rd Dispatch)

(Beiping) People from Rehe talked about the Mengqi organization in Rehe Province, which was originally 13 tribes and 20 banners from the Zhaowuda and Suosutu leagues. After the fall of Rehe Province, the puppet state forced changes to the original organization of the Mengqi, using the Xilamulun River basin as a boundary. Six of the eight tribes and thirteen banners of Zhaowuda and Suifeng in Hebei were divided into the Xing'an West Province, using the false name of Mongolian self-government to divide the unity of the Mongolian and Han ethnic groups. The six banners of the Zhaowuda League and the seven banners of the Suosutu League south of the Xilamulun River, because the Mongolian princes all unanimously refused and opposed the division of the autonomous region, the puppet government feared resistance from the Mongolians, so it temporarily designated the Xilamulun River as a mixed Mongolian-Han area to appease the Mongolian princes. Recently, Songshishi Xiaoliang, the director of the Chengde Special Service Agency, went to the Suosutu League to convene a meeting of Mongolian princes, still advocating to be placed under the jurisdiction of the Xing'an Province. The Mongolians consistently opposed. After deliberation, it was decided to establish a Mongolian Affairs Bureau in the area south of the Xilamulun River, directly under the Xing'an Province, to govern the Mengqi administration and transform the old system of the Mengqi in a disguised form. (3rd Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Central Government plans to form a preparatory committee to handle Inner Mongolian autonomy. Candidates are currently being sought, and will be announced after Huang Shaoxiong and others return to Beijing. Li Songfeng brought the autonomy plan to Beijing. The Central Government has decided to conduct serious diplomatic negotiations with Japan regarding the establishment of an autonomous region in Duolun, following diplomatic procedures. (3rd Dispatch)

Central Government Separately Sends Personnel to Urge Central Committee Members to Go to Beijing; Guangdong Committee Decides to Attend the Fourth Plenary Session 16

(Nanjing) A certain Central Committee member said that the Central Government, with the Fourth Plenary Session approaching, urged all Central Committee members to go to Beijing to discuss major issues together. It has been decided that Zhang Ji will go to Hong Kong to welcome Hu Zhantang, and will leave within days. As for Guangxi, Guangdong, Hebei, Shanxi, and other places, personnel will also be sent to these locations, but the candidates have not yet been determined. The rumor that Hu has other plans is unfounded. Recently, Chen Qingyun, a Central Committee member who came to Beijing and then to Jiangxi, was precisely representing Hu Hanmin to negotiate with key Central Government figures on party affairs issues and major national salvation plans. (3rd Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Southwest Central Committee members decided to attend the Fourth Plenary Session, and Hu also agreed. (3rd Dispatch)

Chen Jitang Telegraphed Beijing Requesting Subsidies for Military Expenses; Requested Permission to Issue Public Bonds; Central Government Considering 17

(Nanjing) After the Fujian Incident occurred, Guangdong Province's military expenses increased sharply, so Chen Jitang telegraphed Beijing requesting subsidies and stated that if there were financial difficulties and there was no way to raise funds, he requested that, following the example of North China, he be allowed to issue 20 million yuan in public bonds, using the Guangdong Customs revenue as collateral. It is reported that the Central Government is considering this request and may submit it to the Central Political Conference for discussion. (3rd Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Of the 30 million yuan in national defense bonds previously issued by Guangdong, only over 4.7 million had been sold as of November. Chen Jitang ordered the Finance Department to stop the sales and handle the closure. As for the expenses for national defense construction, alternative designs are being designed to raise funds. (3rd Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Guangdong Finance Department plans to resume the exchange of 10-yuan banknotes for cash after the one-month period expires. A notice was issued on the 3rd to borrow the rent for all houses and wharves in Guangzhou for one and a half months, with interest at 8%. The cash is used to repay the Guangdong provincial notes. Tenants can use the borrowed rental payment to offset their rent. (3rd Dispatch)

Tibetan Troops Attempt to Advance Eastward; Issue Deadline for Sichuan Troops to Return to All Areas; Otherwise Begin Military Action 18

(Nanjing) Military intelligence reports that about 10,000 Tibetan troops stationed on the west bank of the Jinsha River in western Sichuan recently have plans to seize areas on the east bank of the Jinsha River. It is reported that the Sichuan troops stationed in Kangding are increasingly concerned by the tense situation, and have telegraphed military authorities to request instructions on how to respond. (3rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) There has recently been news that the Dalai Lama's troops are again pressing towards the border of western Sichuan. According to the Liu Wenhui Representative Office, the Kangding County Magistrate of western Sichuan telegraphed Deng's brigade of the Twenty-Fourth Army, stating that the Tibetan forces currently on the west bank of the Jinsha River number over 10,000. To that county magistrate, they requested a deadline of December 2nd for all areas previously recovered by the Sichuan troops to be completely evacuated, otherwise military action would begin. The brigade commander considered the situation urgent and forwarded it to Liu Wenhui, and has now submitted it separately to the National Government, the Military Council, the Executive Yuan, and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission for review and handling. Yesterday was the last day of the Tibetan deadline. Although there is no telegram arriving in Nanjing, it is uncertain if conflict has already occurred, but the situation is truly concerning. (3rd Dispatch)

Frontline Bandit Suppression Victories 19

(Hankou) Remnant bandits on the Henan-Hubei border, led by the puppet military commander Wu Huanxian, held Xuanhuadian East. Xiao Zhichu's troops under Wang's brigade fought hard to recover it, then pursued to Yangjia, killing many bandits. Wu led the remnants to retreat to Dazhuyuan. In addition, the Henan bandit Ma Xiyou's force attempted to flee to Suizao in northern Hubei, but was defeated by Luo Qijiang's brigade, retreating back to Jingbai. After encirclement and suppression, it was completely annihilated in Sishilichong. Xiao and Luo both telegraphed He Chengjun on the 2nd to report their victory. Wang Lingji telegraphed He Chengjun, stating that after the full-line general attack on the 1st, they successively captured Ganshuo, Shuoshanpo, Fuxingchang, Liangfengwo, and Woniushan. Three airplanes dropped 40 bombs at Shuanghekou, killing over a thousand bandits. The pseudo 49th and 29th armies fled back to Suicheng and to the north bank of the Wuqu River. The second and third routes simultaneously captured Hantianda and Tongziyuan, and the sixth route Liao's division also advanced to Fuxingchang to assist in the suppression. (3rd Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Plans to Formulate Measures for Unifying the National Treasury; Four Principles Submitted to the Yuan for Review and Approval 20

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance drafted four principles for unifying the national treasury and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review and approval. The principles are as follows: 1. All revenues directly collected by various ministries and commissions of the Central Government, as well as revenues collected by their affiliated non-profit institutions, and surplus revenues of their affiliated business institutions, or planned appropriations for non-business expenses, shall be submitted to the national treasury for collection. 2. The expenses of various ministries and commissions of the Central Government and their affiliated institutions shall be managed and issued by the national treasury as a whole. 3. Various ministries and commissions of the Central Government and their affiliated business and non-business institutions shall prepare ten-day statements of their business income and expenditures and send them to the Ministry of Finance on a ten-day basis. 4. The Ministry of Finance shall, in conjunction with the relevant ministries and commissions, formulate measures based on the first three principles and submit them to the Yuan for approval and implementation. (3rd Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Decides to Increase Consolidated Tobacco Tax 21

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance decided to increase the consolidated tax on cigarettes, revised the tax rules, and submitted them to the Yuan for approval. The new tax rules will be collected starting from the 5th. The Tax Department of the Ministry has issued a notice stating that from the 5th, domestically produced cigarettes must be affixed with new tax stamps before they can be licensed to leave the factory. Cigarettes that have been affixed with old stamps and left the factory before December 5th are still allowed to be sold. All old stamps purchased and stored by various tobacco companies that have not been used shall be exchanged for new stamps at the same price within 30 days of the implementation of the tax increase. (3rd Dispatch)

Lu Xingrong Enters Hospital for Treatment 22

(Nanjing) Lu Xingrong, commander of the newly organized Second Division, went to Jiangxi to meet with Chiang and request instructions on Zhejiang-Fujian border defense matters. After the matter was completed, he returned to Nanjing. According to Hong Zhongyuan of the division's office, after Lu arrived in Nanchang, Chiang happened to leave for the front, so he reported the current situation of the division in detail to the directors of various departments of the headquarters and requested instructions. He did not stay in Jiangxi for long and took a boat back to Nanjing. Now Lu has a cold and has entered Gulou Hospital for diagnosis and treatment, and will not leave Nanjing for the time being. (3rd Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Orders Hunan Sulfur Mines to Be Changed to Government Sales 23

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance, in order to implement the system of unified government sales of saltpeter and sulfur by the Central Government in all provinces, but Hunan Province still being managed by merchants, has ordered the Hunan Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau to be uniformly changed to government sales. Saltpeter in Hunan is not sold by the government, but sulfur is sold by the government first. The plan is to first purchase the entire monthly output of sulfur and saltpeter from Shuikoushan at a publicly determined standard reserve price and find ways to sell it within and outside the province. The required capital is approximately 30,000 yuan, which will be allocated in installments from the salt tax item based on the actual number needed for deposit in the bank for use, etc. Since Hunan sulfur has been changed to government sales, all previously established Hunan Sulfur Transportation and Sales Offices and Hunan Sulfur Supervisors are no longer necessary and should be abolished. Separate orders have also been issued to the Salt Affairs Audit General Office and the Hunan Sulfur Transportation and Sales Office for compliance. (3rd Dispatch)

Ministry of Interior Explains the Status of Concubines and Child Brides 24

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Interior, in order to explain the status of concubines and child brides, issued a notice to the governments of all provinces and cities, stating that according to the Fujian Civil Affairs Department's report, there are doubts regarding the titles for concubines and child brides in the household survey and requesting clarification. The investigation shows that legally, there is no marital relationship recognized with concubines and child brides. The Ministry of Interior previously responded to a request for clarification from the Henan Civil Affairs Department. As for household surveys, they are based on the number of people currently living together as the members of the household, which is different from the scope of household registration limited to those who belong to the same household. Although concubines and child brides are not recognized legally, they cannot be used for household registration. However, when investigating households, for those who live in the same family with the purpose of permanent cohabitation, they may naturally be regarded as family members in accordance with the Civil Code and entered in the household survey form. (3rd Dispatch)

Revision of the China-Germany Aviation Postal Transport Contract 25

(Nanjing) The China-Germany aviation postal transport contract was signed in 1930 by the Ministry of Communications and the German Lufthansa Company. The capital was 3 million yuan in national currency, divided into 3,000 shares, each with a value of 1,000 yuan. The Chinese side recognized 2,000 shares, and the German side recognized 1,000 shares. Recently, due to insufficient funds to complete the project, the board of directors decided to increase it by 2.1 million yuan, bringing the total capital to 5.1 million yuan. The Chinese and German sides still share the capital according to a two-thirds and one-third ratio, respectively. Now that the capital has been increased, it is necessary to revise the clause regarding the total capital in the China-Germany aviation postal transport contract signed by the Ministry of Communications and the Lufthansa Company. A draft of the Chinese and German clauses has been prepared and submitted to the Executive Yuan for record. (3rd Dispatch)

Shandong Hometown Association in Beijing Relieves Disaster Victims 26

(Nanjing) Due to the Yellow River flood, Shandong, being located downstream, suffered particularly heavy damage. Previously, the Central Government decided to allocate 550,000 yuan for emergency relief to provide food and clothing. However, due to various obstacles, it has not been fully implemented to date. As winter approaches, the weather is cold and windy, and there are still no fewer than 100,000 disaster victims who have no homes to return to. Lacking clothing and food, their situation is extremely pitiful. The Shandong Hometown Association in Beijing has repeatedly received letters and telegrams from all sides requesting assistance. In addition to resolving to petition the government to quickly raise funds for winter relief, the association has also launched a public donation campaign, and has already raised over 2,000 yuan, purchased over 1,600 sets of cotton clothing, and transported them to Jinan in two batches to be forwarded to the disaster victims by the Shandong Provincial Political Affairs Committee. (3rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Hebei Province Coal Mines Classified as State-Run 27

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industries determined that the area of 1,461 hectares, 24 acres, and 72 millimeters of coal mines in the Pengcheng, Xu Kuo, and six other places in the northwest township of Cixian County, Hebei Province, and the area of 877 hectares, 68 acres, and 62.5 millimeters of coal mines in the Shimiao South, Huoyu, Heilongdong, and other places in the same county, and the area of 982 hectares and 8 acres of coal mines in the Dizhai North-South, Huangsha, Laowayu, and Shimiao in the same county have been verified to be suitable for smelting gold and coking bituminous coal mines. In accordance with Articles 9 and 49 of the Mining Law, they should be classified as state-run. The ministry has designated the mining area, and in addition to ordering the competent authorities of the province to register it, it has also submitted it to the Executive Yuan for review and record. (3rd Dispatch)

Bao Yulin Arrives in Beijing 28

(Nanjing) Bao Yulin, a member of the Pacification Army Branch Committee, arrived in Beijing from Jiangxi on the 3rd and will return to Pingjin within days. (3rd Day Special Dispatch)

Current Affairs Commentary

Hirota's Pacific Peace Movement Fails 29

Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota is recently pouring his full energy into employing his peace-making skills. As the New York Evening Post put it, Japan's hope is "Japan's Peace in the Pacific." The paper also stated, "Japan has two hopes. One is to first maintain peace with Soviet Russia, requesting the Soviet Union to remove its military installations along the Russian border. Japan, in turn, plans to abolish its...

military installations in Japanese territory. The intention is precisely to secure the lands it has recently seized. The second is to hope to negotiate naval equality with Great Britain and...

the United States. Furthermore, it believes that China is currently facing many troubles in Fujian, providing an opportunity to take advantage of the tense situation in Europe to pit Soviet Russian interests against those of Great Britain and the United States, thereby reaping the benefits of the fisherman." The conclusion is that it hopes diplomats from various countries can, with astute skills, expose Japan's diplomatic schemes and not fall into their trap. This argument of the paper can be said to have insight into the current situation of the Japanese side. However, from our perspective, it is also overly...

concerned.

Because Foreign Minister Hirota's Pacific peace movement, if it were before the formal restoration of diplomatic relations between the United States and the Soviet Union, might still have had some...

chance of success. Now, no matter how subtle Hirota's skills may be, he has ultimately missed the opportune moment. The deadlock in relations between the United States and Russia over the past sixteen years has been a significant constraint on the diplomacy of both countries. After Japan's invasion and occupation of the four northeastern provinces, Russia demonstrated strength along the northern Manchurian border. However, Russia has consistently used peaceful means to deal with it, even proposing negotiations to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway and further reducing its price. The reason for dealing with Japan in such a perfunctory manner is precisely because the United States had not yet recognized the resumption of diplomatic relations, fearing international isolation, and therefore did not dare to take a hard line. After the announcement of the resumption of diplomatic relations, the Soviet Union immediately stopped the negotiations on the Chinese Eastern Railway and accelerated military preparations along the Russian border. Its determination is clearly visible. Therefore, it can be asserted that it will not be deceived by Japanese diplomacy. The United States' position in the Pacific is extremely important. Since the naval shipbuilding competition in the Pacific began, the situation has become increasingly serious. On the one hand, it is unwilling to easily abandon its promising market in the Far East. On the other hand, it is unwilling to rashly stake its national strength to protect its far-flung colony - the Philippines. Therefore, despite extreme political contradictions with Japan, it is still seeking a way to coexist and make concessions. However, Japan still does its best to develop its original combative instincts and proclaims itself the leader of the Asian Monroe Doctrine, aiming to block the westward expansion of the United States in the Western Pacific. If Japan's plan to dominate succeeds, those who will bear the brunt are not Soviet Russia, which is striving to close itself off and seek temporary self-preservation, nor Great Britain, which uses Hong Kong as its first line of defense and India as its base, but rather the United States of America, which is eager to develop the Far East, support the Philippines, and preserve its naval base on Guam. At this point, the United States must weigh the pros and cons and abandon its past stubborn prejudices against Russia, and suddenly make peace with it. Therefore, the day it resolves to make peace with Russia is the day it resolves to resist Japan.

In recent days, the pro-American rhetoric advocated by Japan has been ignored by American public opinion. Therefore, the Pacific peace movement advocated by Hirota this time is likely to be like a bubble in the air. As for Great Britain and the United States, although they still have some disagreements on economic issues, they are not insurmountable. From a political perspective, their interests are at stake and are bound to converge. Between Great Britain and Japan, Great Britain is deeply suffering from Japan's economic invasion, and almost the entire country is rising up to resist...

Japan's economic power. In this situation, trying to take advantage of the opposition between Great Britain and the United States and Russia to reap the benefits of the fisherman is no longer...

possible. Therefore, we are deeply regretful for Foreign Minister Hirota's diplomatic policy, for having missed the opportune moment.

Japanese Political Situation Turns From Danger to Safety Hirota Devotes Effort to Diplomatic Work Promotes Peace to Actively Break Through Isolation Opinions of Foreign Ministry and Military Not United 30

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota, with the budget issue resolved satisfactorily, will begin the peaceful diplomatic work decided by the previous Five-Minister Conference, starting with frank consultations between Great Britain, the United States, and Japan, as a proposal for the 1935 disarmament conference. The method and timing of the consultations are yet to be determined, but it is hoped that they can be realized within days. (3rd Day Electric Communication)

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota believes that the domestic political situation has stabilized and plans to propose a reorganization plan for the Three-Ministry Liaison Committee to the Army and Navy, making this organ the backing of Foreign Minister Hirota, actively carrying out so-called peaceful diplomacy toward the United States, Russia, and China. It is said that the military's and the Foreign Ministry's diplomatic opinions are still not consistent. The military's diplomatic policy is as follows: (1) A tough policy must be used for diplomacy with Russia, with war as the main and peace as the secondary; (2) Diplomacy with the United States should focus on alienating the United States and Russia and Great Britain and the United States, without actively pursuing peaceful diplomacy and revealing weaknesses; (3) A tough policy must be adopted toward China, with the specific measures as follows:

(1) Assist the National Government, but it is essential to contact local authorities to demand that they recognize Japan's policy toward Manchuria;

(2) The Japanese side agrees to abolish extraterritoriality to contain the China policy of Great Britain and the United States;

(3) Resolve the issues of through traffic and postal service between North China and the puppet state;

(4) Operate aviation businesses between Changchun, Beiping, and Tianjin to obtain aviation rights in North China;

(5) Construct a military railway between Rehe and Beiping;

The Japanese military regards the five items listed on the right as urgent issues to be resolved in its policy toward China, pressing the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to actively negotiate. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' diplomatic strategy toward the three neighboring countries is as follows: (1) Absolutely no war with Russia. Once war breaks out, Manchuria will be in chaos again, prompting a joint effort by Russia, the United States, and China to deal with Japan. Therefore, it is necessary to do everything possible to prevent the deterioration of Japanese-Russian relations; (2) If the United States cancels its extreme attitude toward the Manchuria policy, it will be of great benefit to Japan. Therefore, it is advisable to encourage the United States to invest in the four northeastern provinces and mainland China. Japanese-American cooperation is the only key to resolving the Far East problem; (3) Continue to maintain cordial friendship with France to contain Great Britain's policy toward Japan; (4) Japan must rectify the above-mentioned diplomatic policies, taking confrontation with Great Britain as the best strategy, because Great Britain is easy to strike, but the United States is not easy to break. (3rd Day Chinese United Press Electric)

(Tokyo) In preparation for the 1935 revision of the naval treaty, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will establish a temporary investigation department for arms treaties, requesting new budget items in the ninth fiscal year. The Ministry of Finance also believes that this is a new division of the American Bureau newly requested by the foreign affairs authorities and approves it. At the same time, the authorities concerned also believe that the purpose of establishing the American Bureau and its administrative nature are closely related to the investigation of arms treaties. Therefore, they deeply understand the measures taken by the Ministry of Finance. As a result, the American Bureau is divided into three sections, sharing the investigation of arms treaties, immigration matters, and the systemization of information coordination. Due to budget constraints, the American Bureau will not have a separate director for the time being, and the position will be temporarily held concurrently by Vice Minister Shigemitsu. As for the chief of the Arms Treaty Investigation Section, Mr. Kiyoshi Yamagata, a disarmament treaty expert and currently on leave returning home from his post as First Secretary at the Japanese Embassy in Belgium, has been designated. (3rd Day Electric Communication)

(Tokyo) It has been announced that Minister of the Army Araki has been appointed President of the Imperial Way Morality Association. The association's purpose is to promote the Imperial Way and has an excellent martial arts department. (3rd Day Electric Communication)

Expanding the Authority of the Japanese Ambassador to China 32

According to the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs believes that the independence of Fujian has created a trend for other provinces in China to seek independence. After deliberation by the heads of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, it was unanimously agreed that if Japan's China policy continues to rely on the ambassador to China as the center, as has been the custom, there will be various inconveniences in negotiations when new regimes emerge in various provinces of China in the future. Therefore, it is necessary to take this opportunity to revise and expand the organizational authority of the embassies in China, and to control the diplomatic organs in China in a way that adapts to the new situation, so that when local disputes occur, there is the possibility of rapid negotiation and resolution. The heads of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs have reached a consensus on this view, and Foreign Minister Hirota plans to deploy more capable diplomats to the major cities of Beiping, Shanghai, and Guangzhou, as well as consulates general. At the same time, regarding the anti-Japanese incident in Fuzhou, he is also determined to cooperate with the military to take swift measures to suppress it. (World News Agency)

(Tokyo) Mr. Makoto Yano, a counselor at the Japanese Embassy in China, has already been appointed as the Japanese Ambassador to Chile. The vacancy left by this counselor has been vacant for a long time. Now, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs has transferred Mr. Renzo Sawada, a counselor at the Japanese Embassy in France, to China. He will be ordered to return to Japan and then come to China. (3rd Day Japanese United Press Electric)

Three-Year Plan to Eliminate the Red Flame 33

(Tokyo) The Japanese Ministry of Justice's strategy to eliminate the Red Flame has been decided to be a three-year plan. A concrete plan will be formulated within the year and submitted to the Diet to amend the Public Security Preservation Law, distinguishing between movements that change the national polity and movements that reform the private property system, punishing the former more severely than the latter. If communists repent and reform, they can be released at any time. It is reported that the Ministry of Finance has approved a reform fee of 60,000 yuan for the Public Security Preservation Law, and the Ministry of Finance has also accepted the 146,000 yuan in expenses for the three-year plan to eliminate the Communist Party. (3rd Day China Electric)

The Hague The term of office of Judge Adachi, the Japanese representative to the President of the Permanent Court of International Justice, has expired. Marconi Visits Western Hills 35

(Beiping) Marconi went to visit the Western Hills this morning. Yuan Liangwu hosted a banquet at the Summer Palace. Tonight, He Yingqin will host a grand banquet at Jurentang. Marconi is scheduled to visit the Great Wall and Ming Tombs on the 4th. (1st Day Special Dispatch)

Italy and Russia Begin Talks at the Palazzo Venezia in Rome Involving Both Economic and Political Matters Litvinov Makes a Clear Statement Russia Constrained by Japan Difficult to Fully Focus on European Affairs US-Russia Treaty Does Not Conflict with Italian Interests 36

Rome Mussolini and Litvinov held their first political meeting at the Palazzo Venezia today, lasting seventy-two minutes. After leaving, Litvinov spoke passionately in Russian with the Russian ambassador. Litvinov seemed quite pleased with the results of the discussion. Mussolini will pay a return visit to the Russian Embassy this afternoon, and then continue to meet with Litvinov at the welcoming banquet tonight. Both sides remained silent about the issues discussed and did not reveal them to anyone. It is believed that the discussions included commercial relations between Russia and Italy, disarmament issues, and whether the Soviet Union could join the League of Nations or reorganize the organization. The Italians believe that the restoration of relations between the United States and Russia has greatly changed the Soviet Union's position in the world. Mussolini's invitation to Litvinov to come to Italy was for this reason. It is reported that a communique will be issued tonight, describing the issues discussed by the two leaders. Litvinov has recently attracted attention from the world, and many American and European newspapers have recently published his biography. Litvinov is now fifty-seven years old. In his youth, he was exiled to Siberia for opposing Imperial Russia and was one of the veterans of the Bolshevik Party.

Continuing dispatch It is now believed that Litvinov's conversation with Mussolini today had a dual nature: (1) economic and (2) political. On the economic front, Litvinov stated to Mussolini that the treaties he had negotiated in the United States would not harm Italian interests in any way. As for the political aspect, it is believed that the discussions broadly touched on disarmament matters. It is reported that Litvinov made a definite statement that the Soviet Union is willing to rejoin the European group and participate in future disarmament negotiations both inside and outside the disarmament conference. It is also reported that Litvinov stated that the Soviet Union has always spared no effort in seeking the completion of disarmament, and he also mentioned the tense relations between Japan and Russia, saying that Russia is constrained by this issue in Asia, making it difficult to devote its full attention to European affairs. However, Mussolini's attitude toward this issue has not yet been expressed. (3rd Day Reuters Electric)

A Glimpse of Welcome in Rome 37

Rome After visiting Naples today, Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov went directly to Rome by car, arriving here at 7:40 p.m. Prime Minister Mussolini did not come to the station to greet him. Only Undersecretary of State Suvic and the Italian representative to the League of Nations, Aloisi, along with the Turkish ambassador, were at the station to welcome him. Litvinov was wearing evening dress. After arriving at the station, he took a car to the Russian Embassy. It is said that he will not make any statement about the purpose of his visit before Tuesday. He later told Reuters reporters that he had long cherished the desire to travel, and this time he was able to fulfill his wish, which made him very happy. Local newspapers mostly stated that the main issues for discussion during Litvinov's visit would be trade relations and disarmament. The Vatican newspaper published a headline tonight: "Horrific News of Cannibalism in Soviet Russia." (2nd Day Reuters Electric)

The "Pan-Series Labor Newspaper" is the most interested in commenting, and its discussion seems to imply that Italy can truly understand the value of the Soviet Union and the United States in the issue of disarmament. Italy intends to have the General Committee of the Disarmament Conference recognize the results of the Four-Power negotiations and obtain the prior consent of the Soviet Union, so that it will also agree to these results in the future, to avoid it coming out to obstruct them in the future. The "Pan-Series Political Newspaper" especially drew readers' attention to the common interests of the two countries in the Far East. It said, "Japan seems to want to disrupt the interests of the whole world in the Far East. If Italy cooperates with the Soviet Union, it will definitely produce the best results in the Far East. The economic order that has already been formed in the world will not allow one or two ambitious countries to arbitrarily destroy it. The reason why Italy, Russia, and the United States have reached an agreement is precisely to show this intention to Japan." The newspaper also said that Japan was angry at the League of Nations for not directly supporting Japan's actions in China and therefore withdrew from the League of Nations. "However, the League of Nations, in the name of an international organization, entrusted Japan with the rule of various islands in the Pacific, and the conditions of its rule should be reported to the League of Nations on a regular basis. Now that Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, why have the various islands in the Pacific not been returned to the League of Nations? What is the reason for this attitude? Its daring to do so is precisely because the Japanese believe that the League of Nations and its member states cannot force Japan to return this mandated territory," it said. Major Obstacles to British-Russian Trade Negotiations Have Been Removed Agreement May Be Concluded Soon 41

(London) A diplomatic correspondent for the Sunday Observer claimed to have reliable information that British-Russian trade negotiations have now been completed. The agreement is only awaiting the provisional signing by both parties, and the commercial agreement can be concluded. The main obstacle to these negotiations was the Lena Goldfields Company case (the company suffered significant losses in British capital due to the Soviet government's revocation of mining rights and had claimed £13,000,000 in compensation). The Russian representative has now agreed to negotiate directly with the company representative and seems prepared to provide reasonable compensation. Therefore, this obstacle can be said to no longer exist. However, British people who oppose the resumption of commercial relations with the Soviet Union are still very vocal. Therefore, the commercial agreement is unlikely to be ratified before Christmas. (2nd Day Havas Electric)

Ukrainian Separatist Movement German Aid in Secret Moscow Greatly Shocked 42

(Moscow) Communist leaders now claim that Germany is secretly aiding a Ukrainian plot to secede from the Soviet Union. According to a speech delivered today by Central Political Department member Guo Xio at the Ukrainian Communist Party Central Committee meeting, German Chancellor Hitler's diplomatic adviser Rosenberg, in collaboration with Ukrainian exiles, planned to interfere in Ukraine, sending more than a hundred exiles to infiltrate Ukraine, organize military and terrorist groups, prepare for an uprising, and then follow up with German intervention. These leaders had infiltrated the Communist Party and many held high positions in local governments, secretly communicating with exiles and foreign intelligence agencies on weekdays. Guo's announcement of this separatist movement has shocked the entire Soviet Union. However, according to Communist Party leaders, the Ukrainian separatist movement has been completely wiped out, and it is expected that a considerable number of its key figures have been arrested. (3rd Day National Electric)

Japanese-American Arms Race Japanese Navy Second Replenishment Building Forty-Eight Warships 43

(Tokyo) The navy's budget for next year was decided at a cabinet meeting on the 2nd to be 487 million yen, of which 137 million yen is the new budget for this time. Most of it is based on the Second Replenishment Plan under the London Treaty, to expand the air force and refit capital ships. The overall outline is as follows:

Second Replenishment Plan 44

A three-year project to be continued from 1934 to 1936, with a total amount of 300 million yen, to build a total of forty-eight large and small warships. The cost for the first year is set at 81.8 million yen, divided into the following release warships: (1) Warships built within the limits of the treaty, totaling twenty-two ships, are described below: Type B cruisers, 8,500 tons each, two ships; aircraft carriers, 10,000 tons each, two ships; destroyers, 1,400 tons each, fourteen ships; submarines, 1,900 tons each, four ships; (2) Warships built outside the limits of the treaty, a total of twenty-six ships, two oil tankers, one work vessel, sixteen torpedo boats, four submarine chasers, and aircraft carriers, 10,000 tons each, three ships. The above totals forty-eight ships.

Increasing the Number of Air Wings 45

It has been decided to add eight wings during these three years from 1934 to 1936, with a total cost of 35 million yen, of which 8 million yen will be spent in the first year.

Refitting Warships 46

In 1934, the engines of the capital ships Nagato and Mutsu and the aircraft carrier Kaga will be replaced, with a cost of 43.7 million yen.

Other Land and Sea Equipment 47

A total of 104 million yen for the maintenance of new ships, the rectification of military supplies, the second battery replacement for submarines, large-scale exercise expenses, the maintenance costs of air wings and carrier-based aircraft, and so on. (3rd Day Japanese United Press Electric)

Swanson's Aggressive Policy Intensifies Shipbuilding and Enhances Air Force 48

(Washington) Today, U.S. Secretary of the Navy Swanson, in his annual report to the President, advocated an orderly and aggressive construction of new ships, so that the U.S. Navy can reach the limits of the treaty and become the most effective fleet in the world, and proposed that the United States, in terms of reducing armaments, should give the world a good example. A weak and old navy is enough to hinder world peace, and the U.S.'s foreign policy must also have a corresponding navy as its backing. Although the U.S. Navy has this program to build warships this time, by December 1936 it will only have 113 warships that have not reached their service limit, totaling 988,520 tons. At that time, Great Britain will have 161 such warships, totaling 999,398 tons, and Japan will have 183 ships, totaling 765,370 tons. At present, the U.S. fleet is still 90 ships short of the strength allowed by the treaty, totaling 157,280 tons, while Great Britain is 64 ships short of the strength allowed by the treaty, totaling 197,607 tons. In addition, Swanson also suggested that new aircraft should be built and replace old aircraft in succession within the existing limit of 1,000 aircraft, restore the original salaries of navy and marine corps generals, soldiers, and cancel the 15 percent deduction of vacation pay. Also, within the total shipbuilding program, new ships should be built and replaced old ships in succession, because the operation and victory or defeat of the navy depends on the fleet it has at the start of the conflict. A country's first line of defense cannot be built overnight. He also said that the United States will have six large cruisers, one aircraft carrier, two submarines, and six destroyers under construction by the end of this year. It is expected that twelve new ships can be completed and formed into a squadron in 1934. At present, the navy has 79,200 soldiers, 5,775 officers, and 48,500 non-military personnel. (2nd Day National Electric)

British Guarantee of Air Security General Tone of London Newspapers 49

(London) Gavin, the editor of the Observer, summarized the tone of the Sunday newspapers, saying that they unanimously believe that "hereafter, the issue most directly related to national survival is air security." Although this is the actual situation, the conclusions reached by the steady newspapers on this matter clearly divide public opinion into two trends: "One faction focuses on preventing the danger from the air, and the other does not want to hinder the final success of disarmament." Lord Privy Seal Baldwin and the House of Commons originally wanted to link these two things together, but the newspapers divided them into two. Those who support preparing for air defense include the Sunday Times, which advocates immediate preparation for air defense, saying, "It is not effective to set a ratio for the air forces of various countries, because military aviation cannot be equipped hastily. Therefore, in addition to setting a ratio, the air force should be equipped rapidly at the same time." Observer editor Gavin, a Liberal Party polemicist, advocates a more active approach, saying, "If Britain is strong and unites with its neighbors, war will not occur. Conversely, if Britain is weak and separates from Belgium and France, war may break out. For example, in 1914, if Britain had faithfully adhered to a principle, the World War would have been difficult to occur. What is the principle? That is, 'Maintain the strength of the British Navy, making it three times stronger than Germany's'." The Sunday Times refuted the Observer's argument with the reason often advocated by those who oppose the arms race, concluding that organizing an international air force, or at least reaching an agreement on air force between Britain, France, Germany, and Italy, is the only practical solution, because the ideal of general disarmament is certainly very good, but it is inevitable to seek the next best thing. (3rd Day Havas Electric)

Volcanic Eruption: A Rare Spectacle - Lava Jets Reach Heights of 500 Feet; Underground Roars Heard Miles Away 64

Honolulu. Mauna Loa peak on the island of Hawaii, which has a crater called Moku'aweoweo, suddenly began erupting at dawn today. Accompanied by earthquakes, residents on the mountainside are scrambling to escape. Currently, lava is erupting from fissures two and a half miles from the crater, like fountains. One jet even reached a height of 500 feet. As the lava flows down, the 1,000-foot cliffs inside the crater wall resemble a giant Niagara Falls. Today, airplanes flew over the crater and reported that it was a rare spectacle. The mountaintop is completely covered with volcanic ash, and fruits and vegetables are scorched. The sound of underground roars and erupting smoke can still be heard several miles away. The snow that had accumulated on the summit of Mauna Loa for several weeks has now melted. However, volcanologists now believe that the lava will not break through the crater walls and flow down to bury the coastal towns, as it did in 1926. (Kuomintang telegram, 2nd)

Military Situation After the Fujian Incident - Six Newly Organized Armies, Each with Two Divisions - Establishment of a Propaganda Committee for Unified Propaganda 65

Min Yan She (Fujian People's Speech Agency) Fuzhou dispatch: Cai Tingkai, the so-called commander-in-chief of the First Front Army of the People's Revolutionary Army, and the various army commanders, after taking office on the 25th of last month, Cai immediately consulted with the various army commanders on the new distribution of troops, commanding officers' salaries, the deployment of defenses, and the plan to train troops to attack Zhejiang.

Expansion of Armies 66

Regarding the issue of army subordination, it is reported that each army commands two divisions. The 1st Army, commanded by Shen Guanghan, commands the 1st Division (Liu Zhanxiong) and the 60th Division (Mao Zhicai). The 2nd Army, commanded by Mao Weishou, commands the 2nd Division (Pang Cheng) and the 61st Division (Liang Shiji). The 2nd Army, commanded by Ou Shounian, commands the 3rd Division (Zhang Junsong) and the 78th Division (Yun Yinglin). The 4th Army, commanded by Zhang Yan, commands the 4th Division (Xie Qiongsheng) and the 49th Division (Ruan Baohong). The 5th Army, commanded by Tan Qixiu, commands the 5th Division (Situ Fei) and the 7th Division (Zhao Yijian). It is also proposed to appoint Weng Zhaoyuan as the commander of the 6th Army. It is rumored that Hong Wende and Yu Chengyao will be appointed as division commanders of the 6th and 8th Divisions respectively. The matter will be submitted to the Military Affairs Commission for official appointment within the next few days. As for the 1st Independent Brigade (Chen Qixuan), the 1st Independent Regiment (Nie Jinlong), the 2nd Independent Regiment (Ma Hongxing), the 1st Marine Brigade (Yang Tingying), and the 2nd Marine Brigade (Lin Bingzhou), they are directly under the command of the General Headquarters. A portion of the former 19th Route Army's Special Service Regiment, led by Li Jinbo, is also planned to be expanded into a garrison brigade. It is reported that the General Headquarters plans to reduce the salaries of officers as much as possible, with generals not exceeding 160 yuan, colonels not exceeding 100 yuan, and lieutenants not exceeding 60 yuan. The salaries of soldiers will be appropriately increased.

Chen Brigade Eyes Zhejiang 67

Cai Tingkai, considering the importance of the Fujian-Zhejiang border defense, decided to transfer Chen Qixuan's brigade to the eastern Fujian counties of Funing and others to strengthen the defense. The defense of the Gutian area will be taken over by the 5th Army Commander Tan Qixiu. The 2nd Army (Mao Weishou), stationed in Sha County, will dispatch a portion of its troops to assist in the defense of Yanping. It has been found that Chen Qixuan's brigade has been separately assembled and is awaiting orders to depart, with the intention of attacking the Zhejiang border.

Deployment at Changmen 68

The General Headquarters dispatched staff officers to inspect the fortresses along the coast at Changmen and Mawei on the 24th. They returned to headquarters on the afternoon of the 25th and made a statement saying that the inspection was extremely satisfactory. The mountains and surrounding areas of Changmen are naturally dangerous. In addition to the original fortified artillery positions, which are still solid and can continue to be used, 18 of the latest 1933 Armstrong quick-firing cannons from England have been added, and a large amount of ammunition has been stockpiled. Heavy troops are stationed in various coastal areas, and the defense is extremely tight.

News Policy 69

After the establishment of the so-called People's Government, a Propaganda Committee of the People's Representative Assembly was established. Those in charge are Zhong Xichao, Peng Fangcao, and Hu Qiuyuan of the People's Daily, as well as Chen Weiqi, president of the People's News Agency (formerly the Vanguard News Agency), and Ren Daren, president of the Guoguang Daily. The committee is currently the only propaganda organ of the People's Government. On the evening of the 26th, at 7 p.m., the committee hosted reporters from various newspapers and reporters stationed in Fujian from other provinces in the conference hall (located inside the former Provincial Party Headquarters). Only Cai Xiaogu, a reporter from the Tianjin Ta Kung Pao, and Zhu Jianyu, a reporter from the Hong Kong Huanan News Agency and the Wuzhou Ta Kung Pao, attended from newspapers in other provinces. From the Propaganda Committee, Peng Fangcao, Lin Chongyong, Liu Zhinan, Peng Xinwei, Ren Daren, and Wu Zhixian attended. Peng Fangcao, as chairman, reported on the purpose, roughly saying that there are three points of consideration for today's reception of journalists: (1) From today onwards, this committee will provide news to various newspapers, news agencies, and correspondents stationed in Fujian from other provinces in a systematic manner as much as possible. (2) In the future, the Propaganda Committee is willing to assume the obligation of explaining its attitude towards news. Reporters from various newspapers, news agencies, and correspondents stationed in Fujian from other provinces are welcome to inquire with this committee if they do not understand the news. (3) This committee has recently established a news department to be specifically responsible for liaising with the press. If there are any contacts, you can come at any time. Regarding how the above three points will be implemented in the future, we are extremely eager to know the opinions of the press. Then, Liu Zhinan, the secretary of the Propaganda Committee, spoke, roughly saying that the establishment of the People's Revolutionary Government is by no means the success of the Chinese revolution. It only shoulders the beginning of the crisis of the Chinese nation. Our mission in the future is extremely important, and we must first declare the following matters to you: (1) I hope that reporters from various newspapers and correspondents stationed in Fujian from other provinces will, in the future, stand on the declaration of the rights of the people and the position of saving the country as the basis for compiling reports and issuing manuscripts. If there is any infringement or transgression beyond this basis, this committee will be responsible for correcting and stopping it. (2) In order to facilitate the press and standardize the news, this committee will regularly provide various newspapers and correspondents with news materials as much as possible in the future. (3) In order to establish a close relationship between the Propaganda Committee and the press, the conference has now set up a news department and a news committee, which are headed by Mr. Peng Xinwei. Regardless of day or night, all reporters and correspondents from various newspapers will be given convenience in their contacts. Lin Chongyong then added his opinion, saying that the 19th Route Army accepted the people's request and came to protect the people's rights. I hope that your future remarks will be based on the people's demands. This is not a blockade of speech. The meeting dispersed at 10 o'clock. On the 27th, the news department of the Propaganda Committee also sent a circular to reporters from various newspapers stationed in Fujian, saying: "Dear Sirs, henceforth, for all kinds of news and messages, please send a copy to this department for our reference." (December 1st)

Reorganization of the Peiping Political Readjustment Committee - Added Investigation Department and Construction Discussion Council - Monthly Expenses Increased from 80,000 to 100,000 70

Peiping dispatch: The Central Government recently approved the reorganization regulations of the Peiping Political Readjustment Committee, slightly reducing the internal organization of its affairs, abolishing the Political Affairs and Finance Departments, and also merging the fourth section of the Secretariat. An Investigation Department, a Council Chamber, and the North China Construction Discussion Council were added. In the future, all political and diplomatic measures concerning the journey will first be investigated by the Investigation Department to understand the actual situation, and then the Construction Discussion Council will discuss the plan in detail before it is implemented, so that the Political Readjustment Committee will become like the Governor-General's Yamen of the former Qing Dynasty, but its scope and powers will be further expanded.

After the reorganization order arrived in Peiping, the committee immediately began the reorganization process and officially completed the reorganization yesterday. All personnel were announced at once. Chairman Huang Fu also convened a briefing for the staff yesterday morning. As for the content after the reorganization: (1) The Political Affairs and Finance Departments were abolished, and all affairs were assigned to the first section of the Secretariat for handling by groups. (2) The fourth section of the Secretariat was abolished, and its original functions were merged into the third section. The first group of the first section was merged, and four groups were added to the first section, for a total of three sections and eleven groups. Secretary-General He Qigong and Director Yu Jiaji remained in their positions. Sun Yichen, the head of the first section, and Fu Meng, the head of the second section, remained in their positions. Zhao Zunyue, the head of the third section, was transferred to be an advisor and was succeeded by Zhang Jianchu. Gan Yuli, the head of the fourth section, was transferred to be a secretary, and Secretary He Jiecai also served as the director of the confidential office. (3) A Council Chamber was added, with Wang Kemin as the chief councilor and Wu Jiaxiang, Li Jieyi, Zhang Dongsun, and 33 others as councilors. (4) An Investigation Department was added, with Xu Dingnian and Zhou Yongneng as the director and deputy director, respectively. It was divided into two groups. The first group was responsible for political and diplomatic affairs, and the group leader has not yet been announced, with Liu Shisun being the most hopeful. The second group was responsible for finance and economy, and the group leader was Wang Zemin. Specialists Wang Shimin, Zhou Jingzhan, Zhou Liangcai, and more than ten others served in the first and second groups. (5) The North China Construction Discussion Council was added, with Wang Shuhan, Tang Erhe, and Zhang Zhitam as standing members, and Wang Zhuoran, Qian Jialai, Qian Jinsun, Cheng Xigeng, Li Longmen, Bao Zhusun, Zhao Zhicheng, and others as members. (6) Cheng Ke, Yin Tong, Xu Zhuoran, Chen Juesheng, Pan Zixin, Liu Sirong, Shen Tongwu, Lu Jun, He Cheng, Zhang Xiaoyi, Zhao Zunyue, and sixteen others were hired as advisors. (7) Wei Daofeng, Yin Fuyi, Sun Guofeng, Huang Qiuyue, and twenty others were appointed as counselors.

The reorganization of the Political Readjustment Committee has recruited talents from various factions. The committee's expenses were originally 67,000 yuan and have now been increased to 100,000 yuan. (Reached on December 2nd)

Sichuan Army Launches General Offensive Against Suiding and Xuanhan - Armies Connect and Form Encirclement - Xu Bandits Change Strategy from Attack to Defense - He Bandits Flee Back to the Hubei Border to Join Forces with Xia - 72

Hankou Dispatch: The Sichuan Province bandit suppression military affairs have shown promising progress since Yingshan and Sanhui were successively recovered. According to news gathered over the past few days, the Xu bandits have changed their strategy from fierce attack to firm defense. The eastern route takes Suiding and Xuanhan as its headquarters, concentrating its elite troops there. The mountains of Daxiaopeng and Xiaopeng are also stationed with main forces, with Xindianchang, thirty miles from Yingshan, as the first line and Dachang as the second line. The bandits at Xindianchang are the bandit's puppet fifth army and guerrillas, opposing Yang Sen and Li Qixiang's units. Another major force controls Jiangkou to resist Wang Lingji and Fan Shaozeng's units. The northern route takes Batong as its headquarters, with the Bashan mountain range as its defense line, defending against the Tian and Deng armies. From a global perspective, their momentum seems to have weakened slightly. Currently, Yang Sen's troops have advanced to Xindianchang and are facing off against the bandits. The battles between Longdingguan and Jiulingzi have been fierce for days. Li Qixiang's troops moved forward from Gaofengchang, and Luo Zezhou's troops moved forward from Xujiachang to support Yang's army. Wang and Fan's troops are fiercely attacking Jiangkou, Pujiachang, and other places. At dawn one day, they began a general offensive against Suiding and Xuanhan. A bloody battle is expected to occur in the coming days. After Tian Songyao's troops crossed the Jialing River strongly, they occupied the strategic point of Dadongshan, and Cangxi's defense has become even more consolidated. The line of Zhaohua and Guangyuan is now taken over by Deng Xihou's troops, who need to rest for a few days due to the long journey before launching an attack. From Guangyuan, through Zhaohua, Cangxi, Langzhong, Yingshan, Guang'an, and to Kaijiang, the armies have generally established contact and formed a large encirclement around the bandits. It will be difficult for the bandits to advance in the future. He Long's remnant forces previously fled to eastern Sichuan, while Xia's forces remained entrenched on the border between Hubei, Hunan, and Sichuan. Recently, He Long suffered setbacks in Sichuan and fled back to Hubei, attempting to join forces with Xia, but was unsuccessful. Currently, one force has fled to Dajichang, belonging to Lichuan, and another force has fled to Xiaoguan, belonging to Hefeng. The basic bandits number only 2,000, and the newly formed guerrillas number no more than 1,000. They are being suppressed by Xu Yuanquan's troops. (December 2nd)

Feng Builds a Martyrs' Shrine in Tai'an - Unveiled Upon Completion - Feng Personally Presides Over the Ceremony 73

Jinan Dispatch: Since Feng Yuxiang moved to Tai'an from Chahar, he has not been involved in current affairs. Recently, due to the Fujian situation, rumors spread that he had secretly gone to Fujian, while the Japanese claimed that he had gone to Shanxi in disguise. The reality is that Feng has not left Mount Tai. In order to commemorate Guo Songling, Wang Jinyu, Zheng Jinsheng, Zhang Shaozeng, and others, he purchased one mu of land about half a mile northeast of the Puzhao Temple, where he resides, for 300 yuan to build a shrine for worship. The construction has now been completed, and today (1st) the unveiling ceremony was held. The descendants of Guo and others were invited in advance to participate in the ancestral rites personally presided over by Feng. The shrine gate faces south, and the three houses are of old-style architecture with tiled roofs and stone walls and are not very grand but extremely sturdy. All the arrangements were made according to Feng's intentions. The north house is for Guo Songling, Wang Jinyu, and others, the east house is for Zhang Shaozeng and Guo Songling's wife, and the west house is for Zheng Jinsheng. All use stone tablets, engraved with words and painted vermilion, calling them "Spiritual Tablet of a Certain Martyr." At 9:30 this morning, Feng and more than 200 descendants of Guo and other guests came to the shrine to perform the unveiling ceremony followed by the public sacrifice. They performed the rituals of presenting wreaths as usual. Feng then gave a simple speech, roughly saying that martyrs' shrines are built to commemorate the revolutionary martyrs who died in bloodshed. There are many in various places, but they are still lacking in the north. He built this martyrs' shrine in Tai'an, a scenic area of Mount Tai. The martyrs enshrined in this shrine were loyal and great, rarely seen before. Everyone had a spirit of sacrifice. He personally witnessed them many times in the Luanzhou battle and the Northern Expedition battles. The martyrs died for their country for many years. The purpose of building this shrine today is to mark their memory, comfort the dead underground, and inspire future generations. After Feng's speech, Zheng Jicheng delivered a thank-you speech, and Zhou Baihuang, the magistrate of Taishan County, also gave a speech, expounding the meaning of commemorating the martyrs and praising Feng's thrift in clothing and food to build the shrine to commemorate the martyrs. Then the ceremony ended and the meeting adjourned. (1st)

Anhui Province Borrows Funds to Repair Inland Embankments - Disaster Area Relief Fundraising Committee Formulates Measures - Provincial Government Submits to the Civil Affairs and Construction Departments for Review 74

Anqing Dispatch: The unfinished project of the Anhui Province Jianghuai Main Embankment previously received a reply from the National Economic Council stating that the council had no funds to appropriate and requesting that Anhui Province raise its own funds. The council immediately replied and instructed the counties along the Yangtze River and Huai River to be responsible for requisitioning labor. The "Supervision and Construction Measures for Continuing to Repair the Jianghuai Main Embankment" were drafted and submitted to the Provincial Government Standing Committee for approval and promulgation. Now, the Anhui Province Disaster Area Relief Fundraising Committee has formulated measures for borrowing funds to repair the inland embankments and submitted them to the Provincial Government for review by the Civil Affairs and Construction Departments. The measures are as follows: (1) These measures are limited to the repair of dikes adjacent to the dikes along the Yangtze River and Huai River repaired by the National Government Water Disaster Relief Committee last year, and to the parts of the inland lakes and dikes subsidized by the Anhui Central and Southern Emergency Work Relief Joint Office organized by the committee that have collapsed and are in dangerous locations. (2) If the collapsed dikes in this province meet the provisions of the preceding article, and the arable land within the dikes is more than 5,000 mu, and it can be completed with the amount of the loan to be determined later, the county government may, at the request of the dike residents' representatives or the dike construction committee, formulate a plan and the amount of the loan, submit it to the Construction Department for verification, and forward it to the Provincial Government to apply to the Four Provinces Farmers Bank, the National Economic Council, other banks and silver firms, or other relief agencies. They will be guaranteed by the recovery funds of agricultural relief handled by the China Foreign Relief Committee on behalf of the National Government Water Disaster Relief Committee last year. The county government will repay the loan from the proceeds of the restored dikes in installments based on the benefiting arable land. The repayment period shall not exceed five years. (3) The loan shall be secured by the entire area of benefiting arable land within the dike and guaranteed by the county government, without additional contracts. The amount of the loan shall not exceed 1.5 yuan per mu. The loan certificate shall be signed and sealed by the county magistrate and the dike construction committee, and submitted to the Construction Department for transfer to the Provincial Government, which shall add its seal of guarantee for repayment of principal and interest. (4) If the amount to be paid by the benefited arable land is not paid when due, the arable land will be auctioned by the county government to repay the debt, or if the original owner needs to sell the arable land before the loan is repaid, the debt will be transferred with the arable land and shall be borne by the transferee. (5) Interest rates, repayment periods, and all procedures shall be determined by the Construction Department's order to the county government and the creditor agency through consultation. (6) The repair project shall be supervised by a commissioner appointed by the Construction Department, together with the county magistrate and the dike construction committee, and shall be completed within a time limit. (7) The creditor agency may send personnel to supervise the project and audit the arable land at any time. (8) Detailed measures shall be determined separately by the Construction Department. (9) These measures shall be promulgated and implemented upon the decision of the Provincial Government Committee. (November 1st)

Songjiang Bandit Leader Shi Tang Xiao Di Apprehended 75

Zhang A Xiao (also known as Shi Tang Xiao Di), a notorious bandit from Qingpu Shi Tang who was formerly associated with the gangster Tai Bao A Shu's gang in Pudong, escaped justice after Tai Bao A Shu and others were successively arrested and executed. He repeatedly colluded with Jiangbei gang leader Gao Guiyou (who has been executed) to commit numerous robberies and kidnappings in various towns and villages in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Recently, on August 27th of this year, he again gathered a group to rob the China Merchants Bureau's Hengji steamer at Yu Hui Tang in Zhejiang. On October 12th, he resisted arrest and opened fire on the Ding Zha Changbei team in Dingjia Zha, Zhejiang, killing several team members. Xu Pucheng, the head of the First District of the Jiangsu Provincial Maritime Public Security Bureau, dispatched detectives and ordered a wanted notice to be issued, but the bandit had not been captured for a long time. According to recent reports, the bandit Zhang A Xiao and others had secretly come to Shanghai, planning to collude with accomplices and start a gang in the Dianshan Lake area. However, their whereabouts were uncertain. After Xu, the head of the district, ordered detectives to investigate and determine their address, he secretly ordered team leader Luo Daokun to lead detectives in disguise to keep watch at the address. As expected, they captured the bandit Zhang A Xiao and his wife, Yang Xiubao. They were immediately escorted to the Minhang District Department, where Xu, the head of the district, personally interrogated them. The bandit Zhang A Xiao confessed that in the nineteenth year, he was in the Tai Bao A Shu gang and gathered a group to rob Jinjia Zhuang in Zhejiang. In the Gao Xu battle, he opened fire and resisted arrest with Xu, the head of the district. After being scattered, he repeatedly committed robberies and kidnappings for ransom. The robbery of the China Merchants Bureau's Hengji steamer at Yu Hui Tang was also their doing. Regarding the circumstances of opening fire and resisting arrest with the Changbei team in Dingjia Zha, Zhejiang, he confessed that there were still firearms and ammunition hidden in the straw pile at his home in Shi Tang. Xu, the head of the district, then sent special task force leader Li Quanwu, along with the criminal, aboard the Hongping patrol ship to Zhang Liantang to join the resident detachment and search the premises, seizing eleven various types of rifles and hundreds of rounds of ammunition. His mother, Zhang Qian, was also taken to the district for questioning.

Wuxi Widening of San Xia Tang Street Realized 76

The widening of San Xia Tang Street has progressed from mere talk to a reality. With a designated budget of 18,000 yuan, County Magistrate Yan Shenyu, in order to actively carry out the project, dispatched Qin Xiangtao and Wang Xingzhi, engineers from the Municipal Engineering Department, on the 29th of last month to survey and mark the gray lines and set up central wooden stakes as standards for demolishing and relinquishing the houses on both sides. All procedures are now in place, and it is scheduled to begin automatically demolishing and relinquishing the properties on New Year's Day next year. Those who do not comply will have their properties forcibly demolished by workers hired by the Engineering Department. The residents within the street district do not object, as they believe that the widening will revitalize the market and greatly facilitate transportation. In the past two days, the Qin family's house next to the Xiaolou Lane Embroidery Workshop on the south side, and the Western-style house of Ran Congqiao Gu Zijingxian, have both hired masonry and carpentry workers to demolish and relinquish their properties voluntarily. To avoid disputes, residents Qian Jiqing, Li Shian, Qian Baohua, and others specially convened a meeting of citizens of the street at the Qin Yizhuang on the Dahe River yesterday to discuss and exchange views, expressing unanimous support. In addition to issuing public notices, the county government has also sent letters to each resident, urging them to demolish and relinquish their properties as soon as possible in order to facilitate construction and benefit transportation.

Dai Lane Fire Causes 10,000 Yuan Loss 77

More than ten households, mostly farmers, reside in Dai Lane, near Dongting Town in the tenth district of the county. At around eight o'clock in the morning, a fire suddenly broke out at Dai Afa's house, spreading to neighboring houses on the left and right. The fire was fierce and difficult to extinguish. Residents of the village immediately sounded the gong. Upon hearing the alarm, fire brigades from Dongting, Tingzhuang, Xintang Bridge, Houyang, Jiangxi Bridge, and other places rushed to the scene with water pumps to fight the fire. However, because the flames spread widely, their efforts were futile. The villagers were in great disorder. Fortunately, Chen Yi, the instructor of the Tengchang Township Winter Defense Fitness Exercise Team, led more than ten team members, including Hu Chunyu, to the scene to maintain order. A firefighter, in his bravery to extinguish the fire, knocked down a wall, but the wall collapsed, and he was unable to escape, being buried in the house. Although he was rescued by other firefighters, he was seriously injured. The fire was extinguished after burning for about four hours. Dozens of houses in the village were completely destroyed by the fire, with a total loss of about 15,000 yuan, the heaviest loss being borne by the Dai Sanbao family. The injured firefighter has been sent to the hospital for treatment.

Jiashan County Town Disputes Over Appropriation of Mou Tax 78

Jiashan County is organizing the Home Guard, but due to a lack of funds, it was unanimously decided last winter to levy a mou tax of one jiao per mou to fund the Home Guard's core team. This year, with the addition of the standing team, the funding is even more strained. Unexpectedly, when the mou tax began to be collected, the county government suddenly proposed to appropriate 60% for the county. As a result, the town heads protested one after another. Subsequently, the county party department proposed at the county representative assembly that 70% should go to the towns and 30% to the county, but the county government has not yet agreed. When Civil Affairs Commissioner Lü Michou inspected Xitang, he summoned the town heads for talks and learned that the town heads had asked Lü to resolve this issue.

Jiaxing Fraud Case Appeal Judgment 79

Bao Guifu and his son from Qianliu Township in the seventh district of Jiaxing were previously intimidated and defrauded of 500 yuan by water police investigator Jiang Xianfa in collusion with township head Wang Yuzuo and Peng Yuquan. Afterwards, Bao filed a complaint with the Jiaxing Branch Court, which sentenced Wang Yuzuo to a fine of 300 yuan, Peng Yuquan to 200 yuan, and Jiang Xianfa to two years in prison. Wang and others were dissatisfied and appealed to the High Court. Yesterday, the High Court ruled that Wang Yuzuo would still be fined 300 yuan, Peng Yuquan would be sentenced to six months in prison, Jiang Xianfa's appeal was rejected, and Wang Yuzuo, Peng Yuquan, and Jiang Xianfa should be jointly and severally liable for repaying Bao Guifu 500 yuan.

Nantong Lvsi Two Bandit Leaders Captured 80

Chen Maomao and Lu Shengming, two notorious bandit leaders from Nantong Lvsi, who had committed numerous robberies and crimes, were captured by the police on the second day and escorted to the city for interrogation by the county government.

Highway Robbery Fugitive Apprehended in Shanghai 83
