— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nineteen: Desiring to Depart but Hesitant, Recalling the Past in the Same Car; Half-Crying, Half-Laughing, Leaning on the Pillow in the Lingering Autumn

Speaking in this way, one really shouldn't. One must find this opportunity to say a few words to him. Even if one cannot marry him, one might as well comfort him a little. A woman's heart cannot be shaken; once shaken, there's no way to recover it. Guizhi harbored a sense of indebtedness to Ji Zhi, and she often inquired whether Ji Zhi had any news of returning. In the blink of an eye, it was the summer holidays. Thinking that Ji Zhi would definitely return at this time, she would often pass by the Gan family's door to see if there was any sign of him. Soon two months passed, and the summer holidays were over. It was already the autumn semester. When idle, Ji Zhi also does not return. After the start of school, such a long distance, why does he have to kneel and return? Then he will not be expected. Counting the days, it has been five months since Zhao Ziqiang went to Xifengkou. In those five months, he has sent back over ten letters, about two letters home each month. Although he wrote family letters, much of what he wrote on the letters was to comfort his in-laws. The letter said that he had only received three paychecks, and each time he received a paycheck, he sent them all back, saying that in Xifengkou, there was nowhere to spend the money, and there was a surplus in the office expenses, which was enough to maintain a person's life. Old Man Zhao's attitude was very fair. When his son sent the money home, he would divide half of it to the Yang family. At first, Jiang Shi was unwilling to accept and use it, but Old Man Zhao said that a wedding was definitely going to be held in the second half of the year. Take it and buy some clothing for your eldest daughter to prepare as a wedding dress. Jiang Shi knew that the old man was sincere, so she accepted it. This was in mid-September of the lunar calendar. The weather in the north was slowly getting colder. The sound of cars going to the Western Hills outside the gate was becoming more frequent and lively. It turned out that these were idlers going to the Western Hills to see the red leaves. Every year at this time, they always have to be busy for a while. (258)

Little Common Sense

Air, Wind 193

— Bing Yu

The air surrounding the Earth is approximately four hundred kilometers thick. The pressure of the air is called atmospheric pressure, which varies with time and location. When you hear the phrase "760 millimeters of high atmospheric pressure" on the radio, it means that the average atmospheric pressure at sea level on flat ground. The atmospheric pressure is relatively lower in hotter regions, higher latitudes, and on mountains. For example, at the summit of Mount Himalayas, the average is only about 500 millimeters. This atmospheric pressure means that on average, every square meter of surface is covered by ten thousand kilograms of weight. When foreign children are playing noisily outdoors, their parents often scold them, saying, "Low pressure is coming." This statement has a factual basis, unlike the superstitious peasants in our country who scare children by saying that tigers or ghosts are coming. What is low pressure? It means that rain and snow are coming. These winds, rain, and snow surround the Earth's surface to a height of about fifteen kilometers. Areas of high pressure have a lot of air, while areas of low pressure have less air, but areas with a lot of high pressure are also small. The air in areas of low pressure, whether liquid or gas, maintains its shared property, becoming wind due to the movement of air. However, the changes between high and low pressure are due to unequal temperatures in the atmosphere. The wind varies with the seasons: the gentle spring breeze, the cool summer breeze, the sharp autumn wind, and the fierce winter wind – these are the winds of the four seasons in general. However, the speed of the wind varies: if the wind speed is only 0.3 meters per second or less, the sea surface will not ripple, and the smoke released from factory chimneys will rise straight up. However, the atmosphere is constantly changing, and the wind speed often changes, resulting in distinctions between: (1) breeze, (2) light air, (3) light breeze, (4) gentle breeze, (5) moderate breeze, (6) fresh breeze, (7) strong breeze, (8) near gale, (9) gale, (10) strong gale, (11) storm, (12) hurricane. A breeze has a wind speed between 0.4 meters and 1.5 meters per second, and the smoke from the chimney will be seen to sway. A light air has a speed of 1.6 meters to 3.3 meters per second, and we feel the wind on our faces in the suburbs, and small waves appear on the sea surface. A light breeze has a speed of 3.4 meters to 5.4 meters per second, and when this wind blows, the branches and leaves of trees sway, and hanging flags flutter. A gentle breeze has a speed of 5.5 meters or more and 7.9 meters or less, and when a gentle breeze arises, dust from the ground can be stirred up, and whitecaps appear on the sea surface. A moderate breeze is between 8 meters and 17 meters per second, and when a moderate breeze rises, the leaves rustle as they are blown down, and in the forest, the leaves feel like they are about to sway. A fresh breeze has a speed of 10.8 meters to 13.8 meters per second, and when a fresh breeze rises, the waves on the water surface roll high, and the wires on the utility poles and branches sway up and down and left and right. A strong breeze is faster than a fresh breeze, about 17 meters per second, and when it blows in our faces, it feels like it will blow us over when we were children. A near gale has a speed of 27.8 meters per second, and small branches are often broken by it. Even adults can be blown over, and the waves on the water surface often splash into boats. A gale has a wind speed of about 24.4 meters per second, with the force to break small trees. Ships in harbors must be protected from capsizing, and the roofs of thatched houses are often blown away. The speed of a strong gale is even more severe, between 24.5 meters and 28.4 meters per second. When this wind blows, even large trees are blown down. A storm is even more terrible, with a wind speed of about 33.5 meters per second. Low houses are often blown down, and adults cannot stand on the road. Ships that pass through the sea during a storm are not spared from capsizing, because when a storm arises, the waves on the sea surface are stirred up, coming like an overwhelming force, and are very fierce. A hurricane is the most violent of all winds. Everyone must have understood the damage our country suffered from the hurricane this year. If a steamer at sea sails into the eye of the hurricane, it will either capsize or be lifted high. The above-mentioned twelve types of wind are distinguished according to wind speed. There are other speeds with various names, namely: (1) trade winds, (2) monsoon winds, (3) evening breeze, (4) morning breeze, (5) land and sea breezes, (6) mountain breezes, (7) gusts, (8) tornadoes, (9) breezes, etc. Due to space limitations, I cannot explain them one by one now.

Education News from Other Places

Jiangsu Second District Social Education Research Association Annual Meeting Passes Proposals 194

(Nanjing Correspondence) The Jiangsu Second District Social Education Research Association held its first annual meeting on the morning of the 2nd. In addition to discussing four proposals regarding people's schools and two proposals regarding township improvement associations, as reported previously, there was also a proposal from the Yizheng People's Education Center on how to enable the people to receive a strong influence of civic education. It was resolved that the provincial education center in this district should purchase one or two film projectors to tour the counties in this district to promote propaganda. Regarding cooperative undertakings: (1) the provincial Tangshan Agricultural Education Center proposed actively promoting cooperative undertakings. The following methods were resolved: 1. People's schools should increase cooperative training. 2. Actively compile popular reading materials on promoting cooperative undertakings. 3. Since the Shanghai Bank established an agricultural loan department, other banks such as JinCheng and China Bank also have a tendency to extend loans to rural areas. The funds for cooperative undertakings should not feel lacking again. In order to enable the banks to fully trust social education institutions and the personnel in charge of social education institutions and to be willing to bear this responsibility, it seems necessary to submit a request to the Department of Education to stipulate the term of service for directors of social education institutions. (2) The Tangshan Agricultural Education Center proposed that the funds allocated to people's education institutions should be used for the funds of credit cooperatives. It was resolved to pass the proposal and submit it to the Department of Education to issue an order to the education bureaus and sections of various counties to include this fund in the budget for the next year. At this point in the discussion, there was a break for lunch.

The meeting continued at 2:00 PM to discuss matters regarding agricultural affairs and sideline improvement: (1) "The Tangshan Agricultural Education Center proposed that people's education institutions should organize youth agricultural groups to implement livelihood education." The following methods were resolved: 1. People's education institutions should establish one pilot group among youth chicken farming groups, pig farming groups, cotton planting groups, vegetable planting groups, and chrysanthemum planting groups (except pyrethrum), depending on their own and local environmental conditions. 2. First, connect with the parents of the group members to allocate two square acres of good land to the group members, with a maximum of one acre. If the income from this land is lower than the average income in the area, it should be compensated by the social education institution. 2. All seeds and seedlings shall be borrowed by the people's education institution to the group members. 4. Village elementary school students can be used to organize this type of group (2) The Yizheng People's Education Center proposed how to reduce the difficulties in promoting sideline occupations. It was resolved to handle it according to the local financial situation. (3) How should the fund for the poor people's loan institute be raised? It was resolved that this case could be merged into the case where the funds allocated to the people's education institutions are used for the funds of credit cooperatives, adding the five characters "Poor People's Loan Institute," and no further discussion would be held. (4) Many social education undertakings are of a specialized nature, especially the livelihood education part. In order to achieve practical success, it is necessary to attract specialized talents, but it is not easy to do so due to economic difficulties and meager treatment. How should it be remedied? It was resolved to establish and handle it according to the original plan, and the association will submit a request to the Department of Education for instructions on remedial measures. Then, each case regarding other aspects was discussed: (1) It is proposed that the provincial agricultural education center in this district purchase new agricultural tools and circulate them to various counties for trial use in order to promote them. The following methods were resolved: (1) The provincial Tangshan Agricultural Education Center in this district shall raise funds to implement it. (2) The provincial agricultural center shall appoint staff to various counties to assist in trial use. (2) The association will study and decide that social and educational institutions in the counties under its jurisdiction will jointly purchase art supplies (magic illusion supplies, lantern supplies, film clips, gramophone records, and others). The method was resolved: each county will handle it on its own. (3) The social education institutions in the counties under this research association may exchange, visit, and criticize each other to promote the development of undertakings. It was resolved to pass the proposal. (4) The social education institutions in the counties under this research association will be subject to random selection of staff by the provincial center at any time to go to the provincial center for practice or to organize a visiting group to visit various places to learn from each other and improve undertakings day by day. Passed. (5) In this year's standard work, there are regulations that require each social education institution to promote new agricultural tools. What is the content of this new agricultural tool? Please determine the case. It was resolved to request the Tangshan Agricultural Education Center to investigate and study and then notify the counties to promote it. (6) Hold a livelihood exhibition to tour the counties. It was resolved to request the Tangshan Agricultural Education Center to prepare and carry it out. (7) Please ask the Provincial Education Center to send staff to the counties in this district to assist in promoting livelihood education. Passed. (8) The Provincial People's Education Center proposed dividing districts to implement compulsory education. It was resolved to submit the original proposal of twelve items to the Department of Education to order the counties to try it out in accordance with their discretion. Then, each case regarding administration was discussed: (1) The Jurong People's Education Center proposed that social education institutions in various counties should organize research branches or sub-branches under the system of this association so that they can regularly gather to study various practical social education problems and encourage each other to promote them. It was resolved that this association will submit a request to the Department of Education to notify and implement it. (2) Jiangpu proposed to request the Department of Education to notify all departments to issue social education funds to various counties on a monthly basis to facilitate the progress of undertakings. Passed. (3)

To realize the minimum standard work, the funds for social education institutions in various counties should be unified and averaged. It was resolved to submit a request to the Department of Education to notify the counties to handle it, and explain two points when submitting it to the Department of Education: (1) People's education centers and agricultural education centers should be equally valued. (2) A separate allocation must be made for all education centers that also run libraries and sports fields. (4) Jurong proposed whether social education institutions in various counties can set up quotas for interns to recruit junior high school graduates or above, and provide them with appropriate training to achieve the dual benefits of cultivating talents and assisting in social education. It was resolved to submit a request to the Department of Education to stipulate the methods. 5. The Tangshan Agricultural Education Center proposed to request the Department of Education to issue an order to various counties to establish agricultural and forestry supplementary schools to cultivate out-of-school youths in rural areas. Passed. (6) Jiangpu proposed to request the Department of Education to set up short-term handicraft training centers so that social education institutions in various counties can send staff to study. It was resolved to amend it to "Submit a request to the Department of Education to set up agricultural product manufacturing handicraft training centers so that social education institutions in various counties can send staff to study." Passed. (7) Submit a request to the Department of Education to promulgate compulsory literacy methods for the masses to facilitate popularization. It was resolved to handle it in the compulsory education plan that had been previously discussed. Then, each case regarding association affairs was discussed: (1) The Provincial Beijing Center proposed to draw up a draft of the organizational charter of the association and request review. Passed (2) The Provincial Beijing Center drew up a draft of the association's communication research methods and requested review. Passed. (3) Please determine the location and date of the next congress convening agency. It was resolved to hold the second congress in Tangshan in mid-October and invite the provincial Tangshan Agricultural Education Center to convene it. (4) Please determine the central research question for the next congress. It was resolved that the next congress would focus on livelihood education as the central research question (5) What kind of activities should the next congress hold? Please decide publicly. It was resolved that the next congress will hold lectures and exhibitions related to livelihood education. (6) The Social Education Research Association in the Fourth District launched the organization of the Jiangsu Social Education Research Association and intended to send a brief introduction to solicit consent. How should it be handled publicly? It was resolved to accept the principle. Then, temporary motions were discussed: (1) The Tangshan Agricultural Education Center proposed to organize the Cooperative Undertakings Promotion Committee in this district. It was resolved that one person will be recommended by the Provincial Social Education Institution and one person will be recommended by each county, and a number of honorary members will be invited to organize it. The person from each county will be designated by the Education Bureau, and the honorary members will be invited by the Provincial Social Education Institution. The discussion concluded at 5:00 PM. All proposals had been completed, so it was decided to spend another hour discussing the central research question that had not been completed yesterday, focusing only on discussing people's schools, and leaving livelihood education for the next congress to research. The other questions were limited by time, and the Provincial Social Education Institution will study them through communication in the future. The research on people's schools will still use the methods drafted by the Provincial People's Education Center as a blueprint, and the written opinions proposed by the counties will be incorporated. Generally, the methods have been decided. In the evening, Chen Jianxiao came to the meeting to give a lecture and show educational films, and it ended late at night.

Correction: Yesterday's newspaper published a section that combined the case that social education institution staff should closely contact local agencies and people in order to promote social education undertakings with the case on how to enable the people to receive a strong influence of civic education. This was because the association's review report did not correct the numbering of the cases in the proposal (there were two twelfth cases), which caused the reporter to miswrite. The correction is as follows: "Determine the ways in which social education institutions in various counties contact public service or autonomous institutions, and that staff of social education institutions should closely contact local institutions and people in order to promote social education undertakings. The previous case was merged into the previous case and resolved. The association will submit a request to the Department of Education to notify the county governments to instruct the agencies under their jurisdiction to assist in the process."

Organizational Charter of the Jiangsu Second District Social Education Research Association Appendix: Draft Organizational Charter of the Jiangsu Second District Social Education Research Association Passed at This Congress 195

1. This charter is formulated based on Article 2 of the Regulations on the Jiangsu Provincial Social Education Zonal Research Association promulgated by the Department of Education. 2. This association is named the Jiangsu Provincial Second District Social Education Research Association. 3. The purpose of this association is to study social education issues and promote the development of social education undertakings in this district. 4. This association is organized by the Provincial Nanjing People's Education Center, the Provincial Tangshan Farmers' Education Center, the education bureaus of Jurong and Jintan counties, the county governments of Jiangning, Jiangpu, Liuhe, Yizheng, Lishui, and Gaochun counties, and the county-level people's education centers, farmers' education centers, and people's education experimental areas in the district. 5. The handling of association affairs adopts a value-year system, which is taken care of in rotation by the Provincial Nanjing People's Education Center, the Provincial Tangshan Farmers' Education Center, the education bureaus or county governments of the counties in the district. 6. The research matters of this association are stipulated as follows: (1) matters concerning guiding the popularization of social education in various counties, (2) matters concerning promoting the development of social education in various counties, (3) matters concerning social education improvement plans and implementation methods, (4) matters concerning the advanced study and training of social education personnel, (5) matters concerning the use of holidays to hold seminars and training courses, (6) matters concerning social education investigation, statistics, and reporting, (7) matters concerning the publication of social education publications, (8) matters concerning the inspection of the implementation of social education in various counties, (9) other matters concerning social education research. 7. This association holds a congress once a year. Each participating organization must send one representative to attend, but when necessary, it can apply to the Department of Education for suspension. The Provincial Nanjing People's Education Center and the Provincial Tangshan Farmers' Education Center will separately gather the directors and staff of social education institutions in one county or several nearby counties to hold a meeting to study various special and difficult issues. 8. The location and date of the congress of each session of this association shall be decided by the convener of the previous congress. 9. The research questions of each session of this association shall be solicited by the value-year institution two months in advance. The central research question shall be decided by the previous congress. 10. This association may conduct communication research, and the detailed methods will be formulated separately. 11. The funds of this association shall be shared equally by the Provincial Nanjing People's Education Center, the Provincial Tangshan Farmers' Education Center, and the county education bureaus or county governments in the district, but the amount shall be between 10 and 15 yuan per year. 12. This charter shall be submitted to the Department of Education for record after being resolved by the first membership congress of this association.

Ministry of Education Revises Regulations on Secondary School Graduation Joint Examinations and Regulations on Secondary School Graduation Joint Examination Committee 196

The Ministry of Education revised the regulations on joint graduation examinations for primary and secondary schools. As recorded in this newspaper on the 2nd, the ministry promulgated the regulations on joint graduation examinations for secondary schools and the regulations on the committee on joint examinations. At the same time, it issued an order to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to comply. As for the joint graduation examination for primary schools, it may be temporarily exempted. The order states: "It is hereby ordered that the interim regulations on joint graduation examinations for primary and secondary school students have been revised by this ministry into regulations on joint graduation examinations for secondary school students. The regulations on the secondary school student graduation joint examination committee have been formulated separately. In addition to issuing the order separately, we are issuing one copy of each of the relevant regulations. You are ordered to comply." Attached are the regulations on joint graduation examinations for secondary school students and the regulations on the secondary school student graduation joint examination committee.

Regulations on Joint Graduation Examinations for Secondary School Students 197

(Article 1) The educational administrative organs of each province and city shall conduct joint graduation examinations for the graduating students of the secondary schools under their jurisdiction after they have been examined and passed by the original school in accordance with Articles 59 and 60 of the secondary school regulations.

(Article 2) The joint graduation examinations for public and registered private secondary schools in provinces, counties, and cities shall be handled by a committee organized by the educational administrative organs of each province. The joint graduation examinations for public and registered private secondary schools in cities (municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan) and districts (special administrative regions) shall be handled by a committee organized by the educational administrative organs of each city and district.

(Article 3) The regulations on the committee on joint graduation examinations for secondary school students shall be determined by the Ministry of Education in a separate order.

(Article 4) The subjects of the joint examination are tentatively set as follows: (1) Senior high school: Civics (those grades that have not implemented the newly promulgated secondary school curriculum standards will still take the Party Principles), Chinese, Mathematics, Physics, Chemistry, Biology, History, Geography, Foreign Language. (2) Junior high school: Civics (those grades that have not implemented the newly promulgated secondary school curriculum standards will still take the Party Principles), Chinese, Mathematics, Science (Physics and Chemistry), (Biology, Zoology, and Botany), History and Geography, Foreign Language (those grades that have not implemented the newly promulgated secondary school curriculum standards in the third grade who elect to study vocational subjects should take the vocational subjects).

(Article 5) Schools participating in the joint examination should hold a graduation examination within two weeks before the date of the joint examination.

(Article 6) One month before the joint examination is held in each area, each school should submit a list of graduating students with photos to the competent educational administrative organ, and the graduation grade report for each subject should also be submitted before the start of the joint examination.

(Article 7) The calculation method for the grades of each subject in the graduation joint examination should be based on the graduation grades of each subject in the school (the academic year grade of each subject accounts for three-fifths of the graduation grade of each subject, the graduation examination grade of each subject accounts for one-fifth, the joint examination grade of each subject accounts for six-tenths, and is calculated together. (The above grades are all calculated as a percentage, and six-tenths is the passing standard.)

(Article 8) Graduation joint examinations in various places should be held in the last week of June and the first week of January each year. The examination location should be determined and announced by the competent educational administrative organ. In areas with a wider area and more students, for the convenience of students, the examination should be divided into districts, but the prescribed date must still be followed. The examination questions shall be drawn up by the question-setting committee of the examination committee, and the examination papers shall be prepared by the competent educational administrative organ and sealed.

(Article 9) If a student cannot participate in the joint examination due to illness or other reasons, the original school shall investigate and verify the facts and submit a certificate. With the approval of the joint examination committee, the student may take a make-up examination. The date of the make-up examination shall be determined by the committee.

(Article 10) Students must pass all subjects in the graduation joint examination to graduate. Those who fail three or more subjects shall be ordered to repeat the grade, but the number of times repeating the grade is limited to two. Those who cannot repeat the grade due to circumstances may be given a certificate of completion by the original school, stating the grades of each subject in the graduation joint examination and indicating that the joint examination failed. Those who fail two or one subjects in junior high school shall be allowed to participate in the next joint examination of the subjects, and they can graduate only after passing. Those who fail two or one subjects in senior high school shall be allowed to participate in the next joint examination of the subjects. Those who wish to continue their studies may be issued a certificate of registration for further studies by the competent educational administrative organ, stating the grades of each subject in the graduation joint examination, allowing them to take the entrance examination for further studies first. After being admitted, they shall be allowed to be probationary students. They shall not be considered official students until they pass the next joint examination of the subjects and obtain a graduation certificate.

(Article 11) The educational administrative organs of each province and city shall announce the results of the joint examination within two weeks after the joint examination and issue a certificate of passing the graduation joint examination.

(Article 12) At the end of the joint examination, the average of the grades of each subject in the graduation joint examination obtained by each student shall be classified into levels for disclosure. At the same time, the ratio of the number of graduating students in each school to the number of participants in the joint examination and the ratio of the number of participants in the joint examination to the number of passers of the joint examination shall be separately listed as four levels: A, B, C, and D. Then, the average number of students passing the joint examination in each school shall be divided into four levels: A, B, C, and D for disclosure.

(Article 13) The ranking of students in each school shall still be arranged by each school according to the graduation grades of each student in the school.

(Article 14) Before holding the secondary school graduation joint examination, the educational administrative organs of each province and city shall submit the examination location, the list of committee members, and the handling procedures to the Ministry of Education for record. They shall also submit the students' joint examination grades, the level of the participating schools, and the handling process to the Ministry of Education for record within one month after the end of the examination.

(Article 15) The educational administrative organs of each province and city shall be strictly confidential when handling the joint examination. If there is any leakage of examination questions or other fraudulent activities, they shall be punished according to law.

(Article 16) The educational administrative organs of each province and city shall strictly verify the students' usual grades, grades for each semester, and grades for each academic year of the secondary schools under their jurisdiction. If any illegal or favoritism is found, the whole or part of the grades shall be denied, and the responsible personnel shall be punished.

(Article 17) If the educational administrative organs of each province have special difficulties for the graduating students of the junior high schools under their jurisdiction, after being approved by the Ministry of Education, they may select a part of the junior high schools in the province to hold the joint examination, but the number of schools selected for this examination must account for more than one-half of the total number of junior high schools in the province.

(Article 18) These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Regulations of the Middle School Student Graduation Examination Committee 198

(Article 1) These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 3 of the Middle School Student Graduation Examination Regulations.

(Article 2) The Middle School Student Graduation Examination Committee shall be organized by the education administrative authorities of provinces, cities, and districts.

(Article 3) The Middle School Student Graduation Examination Committee shall have six to twelve members, who shall be appointed or hired by the education administrative authorities of each province, city, and district. The head of each of these authorities shall serve as the chairman of the committee. In cases where examinations are held in different districts, a chief examiner shall be appointed to preside over the examination affairs of one district and may appoint personnel from the education administrative authorities of neighboring counties and cities to assist in the handling of matters.

(Article 4) The Middle School Student Graduation Examination Committee shall establish question-setting committee members and proctoring committee members to separately administer the matters of question-setting and proctoring. None of the aforementioned committee members may be teachers or staff from the schools participating in the examination.

(Article 5) The Middle School Student Graduation Examination Committee shall have a number of staff members, who shall be appointed by the heads of the education administrative authorities of each province, city, and district from among the staff members of their respective agencies and directly subordinate agencies. All positions shall be unpaid.

(Article 6) The Middle School Student Graduation Examination Committee shall be established one month before the date of the examination and shall be dissolved upon the conclusion of the examination affairs.

(Article 7) Appointed members of the Middle School Student Graduation Examination Committee may be given appropriate subsidies.

(Article 8) All matters listed below must be resolved by the graduation examination committee and then decided by the chairman: (1) Formulation of various examination rules; (2) Review of the graduation scores of students participating in the examination; (3) Decisions regarding graduation, retention, and make-up examinations for each student participating in the examination; (4) Matters concerning the calculation and publication of examination scores; (5) Other important matters concerning the examination. Examination affairs, with the exception of the matters listed on the right, shall be handled by the committee staff under the direction of the chairman.

(Article 9) Meetings of the Graduation Examination Committee shall be convened by the chairman, who shall also serve as the chairperson.

(Article 10) Middle School Student Graduation Examination Question-Setting Committee members shall be hired by the education administrative authorities of each province, city, and district from among those with rich knowledge and teaching experience.

(Article 11) The powers of the question-setting committee members shall be to draft twice the number of test questions for each subject (to be selected by the chairman), to draft standard answers, and to serve as graders of the examination papers. Question-setting committee members shall be responsible for strictly maintaining the confidentiality of the questions.

(Article 12) The content of the examination questions for each subject of the graduation examination shall comply with the following standards: (1) It should be based on the syllabus of each subject in the curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry (for grades that have not implemented the newly promulgated middle school curriculum standards), it should be based on the graduation (minimum) standards of each subject in the provisional standards; (2) It should include the entire content of the teaching materials for each subject; (3) It should focus on the teaching materials in each textbook and avoid obscure or ambiguous questions; (4) Questions, with the exception of foreign languages, should be in Chinese, and the number of questions requiring answers in each subject should be estimated based on the time allotted for the examination of that subject.

(Article 13) The chairman shall be responsible for the safeguarding of matters such as the setting and printing of examination questions.

(Article 14) Detailed rules for the operation of the committee shall be formulated by the education administrative authorities of each province, city, and district.

(Article 15) These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Sino-French Friendship Association Established Yesterday to Promote Sino-French Culture; Chu Minyi and Wang Jingqi Elected Directors 200

The Sino-French Friendship Association is jointly organized by students who have returned from studying in France, Belgium, and Switzerland, graduates of French language schools in China, and French citizens residing in China. Its purpose is to connect feelings and promote Sino-French culture. The association held its inaugural meeting at the French Association on Rue du Consulat yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan, and Zeng Zhongming, Minister of Railways, sent congratulatory telegrams. Details are as follows:

Attending Members 201

Those present yesterday included Chinese members Chu Minyi, Wang Jingqi, Geng Jiaji, Zhu Yan, Jiang Wenxin, Nong Ruhui, Lin Jun, Xie Shou Kang, Zhang Junqi, Zhang Yinong, Ms. Wang Mingmin, and French members Mr. Li Ang, Consul General Ge Fa, Dr. La Bao Te, Mu Jing, Dr. Song Deli, and over a hundred others.

Preparatory Process 202

The temporary chairman, Laimai, first gave an economic report by Ruosibo, followed by a report on association affairs by Gaoboai, stating briefly that the association established a preparatory committee in mid-July of this year and began operations in mid-October. The initial founders numbered only fifty, but the current membership has reached one hundred and ninety. However, because few people outside know about it, many have not yet joined. The organizational purpose of this association is to promote Sino-French friendship and communicate Sino-French culture. It is purely a cultural organization. In the future, it is hoped that there will also be corresponding members in Europe. Today's establishment of the association has been greatly supported by French Ambassador Weili Deng, Consul General Meiliai, President of the French Association Lirong, and important figures of the Chinese government, such as Wang Jingwei and Zeng Zhongming. The encouragement from all sides will ensure the hope of success in future work, he said.

Election of Directors 203

After the articles of association were revised and approved, the election of directors took place. Those elected as Chinese directors were Wang Jingqi, Wei Yu, Chu Minyi, Song Wusheng, Hu Wenyao, Jiang Wenxin, Wu Zhihao, and Li Zhangyang. Those elected as French directors were Gaoboai Yashibo, Bairongzhang, Bali, Xigu, Puluo Ruo, and Yaming Naweibin, totaling sixteen directors. Zhu Yan, Zhao Wu, Nong Ruhui Lin, Zu Qin, Pan Zhaobang, Xiong Kexiang, Shideer, and Degu Di were elected as alternate directors.

Tomorrow marks the eighteenth anniversary of the Zhaozhong warship uprising. Zhaozhong Middle School on Avenue Haig in this city plans to expand publicity and commemorate its founding. It originally intended to hold a grand commemorative meeting at the Chen Ying Shi Memorial Hall in the Hushi on Guizhou Road tomorrow, along with recreational activities. All preparations had been completed. Doctor's Ability and Satisfactory Medical Skills 235

— Xie Yunshou

Nowadays, it is common to see lawsuits between patients and doctors in newspapers. The court's judgments often result in non-prosecution, which proves that the doctor did not make a mistake. If there was no mistake, why did it lead to a lawsuit? I think that apart from "genuine mistakes," the remaining reasons for lawsuits are nothing more than two: one is a dispute over emotions, and the other is dissatisfaction with medical skills. The so-called dispute over emotions is a separate issue and not related to this article. What we want to discuss now is the patient's dissatisfaction with medical skills.

Ordinary patients, when they get sick and seek a doctor, believe that the doctor always has a solution. They even superstitiously believe that a certain disease is born with a certain medicine, which is the so-called "every disease has a medicine, and no ghost can escape death." Therefore, when they first seek treatment, they praise the doctor to the extreme. But when they die from the disease, their relatives and friends will definitely have a lot to say, either that the medicine was bad or that the surgery was bad. This is really because people overvalue medical skills. Because they overvalue it, when they encounter a disease that cannot be cured, they develop a sense of dissatisfaction with medical skills. People whose emotions are easily impulsive will make a scene that leads to a lawsuit.

What is considered satisfactory medical skill? I think it is difficult for anyone to make a definite statement. Now I will first write down the doctor's abilities below, and then discuss what is considered satisfactory medical skills.

(1) The doctor can recognize the disease. Based on their knowledge, experience, and the help of medical equipment, doctors can recognize diseases. For example, in the same case of fever, the doctor can know that A's fever is pneumonia, and B's fever is malaria. In the same case of abdominal pain, the doctor can know that A's abdominal pain is appendicitis, and B's abdominal pain is ordinary enteritis.

(2) The doctor can treat the disease. After recognizing the disease, the doctor can use medicines and surgery to treat the disease. For example, diphtheria is treated with diphtheria antitoxin, syphilis is treated with Salvarsan, and appendicitis is treated with surgery to completely cure the disease and restore the patient to health.

(3) The doctor can alleviate the patient's suffering. There are many diseases that are beyond the reach of current medical capabilities, such as severe pulmonary tuberculosis and metastatic cancers. Although doctors cannot completely cure the original disease, they can find ways to alleviate the patient's suffering. In addition, using prosthetic legs and arms to replace real legs and arms, and using artificial eyes to decorate the appearance are all methods of doing the best one can in a difficult situation.

(4) The doctor can prevent diseases. Doctors have the knowledge and ability to prevent diseases. For example, they know how to prevent smallpox by vaccinating, and how to prevent cholera by administering cholera vaccines. They know how infectious diseases are transmitted, and tell everyone how to pay attention. They know that scarlet fever can be followed by kidney inflammation, and that typhoid fever can be followed by intestinal bleeding and intestinal perforation. When blood pressure is too high, stroke should be prevented. The doctor not only tells the patient to pay attention in advance, but also finds ways to prevent it.

(5) The doctor can determine the prognosis. For example, a disease may have a very dangerous appearance, and another disease may have a very peaceful appearance. The doctor can determine that although the first disease is dangerous, there is no need to worry, while the second disease, although peaceful, is worrying. Also, for metastatic cancers and appendicitis that has become diffuse peritonitis, the doctor can know in advance that the prognosis is poor.

Are the above enough to be considered satisfactory medical skills? Even I dare not answer yes. Moreover, what doctors can do is often affected by the myriad changes in personnel, the different environments, the severity of the disease's virulence, the patient's resistance, the presence or absence of specific constitutions, and the occurrence of unexpected events. The results of disease treatment are not necessarily constant. Therefore, even if preventive work is done, the disease still occurs. A mild cold can suddenly turn into pneumonia, typhoid fever can suddenly lead to intestinal perforation, the use of quinine can lead to blackwater fever, and the use of serum can lead to serum sickness. Death can occur from general anesthesia and death can occur from injections of 606. Even famous surgical masters have patients who die from surgery. From the patient's point of view, this is poor medical skill, but in medical terms, it is called surgical misfortune or an occasional complication, which is something that human power cannot recover. In ancient times, there was a famous Roman doctor named Galen. He had a saying, which I will now introduce below:

"The reason why diseases are cured is not by the hand of the doctor, but by the power of natural spirit (Spritus Natuz ralis, Preurna Pbysikon). The doctor is only helping nature to remove the harmful conditions to the disease."

Now that we know the doctor's abilities as described above, and have read Galen's remarks, we can know that it is difficult to have satisfactory medical skills in the world. Therefore, as long as the doctor is not wrong from the standpoint of medical theory, he can be free of conscience.

The Crisis of Lung Disease in China and the Urgent Plan for Today (Part 1) 236

— Ding Huikang

Considering the most prevalent diseases in our society, the spread of lung disease is undoubtedly one of the most serious problems. However, in reality, lung disease is not necessarily an incurable disease, but a curable disease. The reasons why it is rampant and cannot be contained are approximately several:

(1) The Chinese people lack basic health knowledge. There is a risk of infection anytime, anywhere.

(2) The Chinese people lack basic medical knowledge. When the initial symptoms of the disease are very mild, they are often ignored, and the treatment method is unknown, so most patients lose the period when treatment should be given.

(3) Excessive faith in doctors. Because the Chinese people lack proper concepts, they procrastinate when they get sick, and often cannot solve the problem thoroughly. Once they invite a doctor to examine them, they regard it as having done everything they can and ignore all other more important recuperation methods.

(4) Belief in the omnipotence of medicine. To this day, it has been recognized by the medical community worldwide that "there is no specific medicine for lung disease," but most patients are smart and think that lung disease is a chronic disease and only needs to be treated with medicine. Therefore, if taking medicine A is ineffective, they switch to medicine B. If that is also ineffective, they buy medicine C and take it. In this way, they repeatedly delay, and unconsciously, the disease becomes severe. Only then do they begin to recuperate, but it is too late.

There are many reasons for the large number of lung disease patients in China today, which, in short, are approximately as described above. However, it is not too late to mend the fold after the sheep is lost. Where is the remedy?

(1) The state should establish a lung disease research institute.

The lung disease research institute must hire domestic and foreign experts to preside over it. All methods for clarifying the cause of the disease, the implementation of public health, the execution of isolating patients, and the research of preventive vaccination and effective drugs are the main tasks. This great undertaking related to the health of the nation, given the social conditions in our country and the large number of lung disease sufferers, it would not be an exaggeration for the state to allocate tens of millions or hundreds of millions in funding annually for specialized research. Unfortunately, China's construction is lagging behind in everything. Not only is there no funding in the government, but there is also a lack of specialized talent. Even if there is, they can only start a business and make a living. Those who can diligently devote themselves to research for the benefit of the country and the people, the truly great medical scientists, are as rare as phoenix feathers in China. Therefore, the establishment of a lung disease research institute is currently an impossible reality. I have no choice but to consider the next best thing. (2) Health education should be popularized and physical fitness should be emphasized.

Education in our country cannot be popularized, so most people lack health and medical knowledge. For the present, public health and basic medical knowledge should be included in the curriculum of existing schools, so that everyone can understand the methods of disease prevention and the main points of treatment. Those who study today want to apply what they have learned to the world in the future. The body is the foundation of learning. How can these important knowledge related to life and health not be instilled? There is no shortage of students who are diligent and persistent, but who die of lung disease after graduation. How sad it is to let such talents be buried. Therefore, the health and education authorities should properly discuss the curriculum on health, medicine, and physical fitness. It is difficult to see any results at present, but in the future, the results will be significant. When education is popularized throughout the country, the day of successful prevention of lung disease will be inevitable. But this is only in terms of preventing lung disease. As for eradicating lung disease, it is necessary for patients to have considerable medical knowledge. What is the method? Let me try to state my humble opinion.

(3) Each county and district should establish more lung disease prevention research associations to popularize the knowledge of prevention and treatment to the public in simple terms, so that the healthy can know how to prevent it, and the sick can know the correct treatment method, so as not to be misled by quack doctors and fake medicines. This is the best way to save oneself and put out the fire.

Shanghai is the center of the medical community in our country. Only this year did Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Director Li Tingan initiate the establishment of an anti-tuberculosis association for this important issue, which is a somewhat comforting move for the people. However, how to solicit members and how the association's affairs will be conducted have not yet been reported, or perhaps it has not been established for long, and all matters are waiting to be planned and implemented.

The Origin of Pharmacognosy (Continued) 237

— Zhao Qiong Huang

In the era of Western materia medica, after Dioscorides, Galen (Galenusi 130-20 A.D.) was born and enjoyed the honor of being a famous doctor for a time. Pliny the Elder (Clinius Secundue 23-79 A.D.) and Encyclopedis were also born during that time. From the third century A.D. onwards, from Oribasius Ca 325-400 A.D. downwards, the number of well-known people gradually decreased. It gradually entered the Middle Ages. In the Dark Ages, there were almost no records of scientific value. Fortunately, after leaving the Dark Ages, the Renaissance of Greek and Roman literature and art was remembered, and talents emerged in large numbers. Among the Arabs, there were many who passed on the mantle of Dioscorides, such as Trasillus. Botanists such as Brunfeis (1498-1544), Fookes, and Tragis were called the three fathers of German botany, and Valerius Cordusi 515-1544 wrote "Historia Stilium" (1519 edition), which established its scientific foundation. Materia medica experts such as Avicenna and Serapion Ca 1110 also gathered between the 10th and 15th centuries. Scholars such as Ibn Baithar +1248 followed one after another. At that time, books on materia medica circulating on the market were selling

Page 14

extremely well. The content and level of the materia medica books were similar to the "Shen Nong Ben Cao Jing" (502 A.D.) revised by Tao Hongjing in our country. Works that have been reprinted dozens of times, such as Macor Floridus Arald Villanova Platoariolamily, Abortus Magnus, etc., are even better than our country's materia medica books. The dictionary of medicinal plants by Mattes Plateario II (completed around 1134), "Circe Instans," was the most popular materia medica book at the time. The abridged materia medica compiled from it once swept the world. Among them, the illustrated descriptions of animals, plants, and minerals, reprinted dozens of times, are the Ortus sanitatis by an anonymous author (the first edition was probably before 1475), and its translation of Johan von Cuba Gartdor Gdeundbeit (1458 edition) and its variant, the Kreutterbuch (1533 edition), etc. Also, La Grant Herbicren francoys (1490 edition) in France and its reprinted editions. The English translation of Tho Grete Herbal (1516 edition) and its reprinted editions, etc., are truly too numerous to mention. Since then, the writing of such popular materia medica books, using the name Herbal (materia medica), has gradually become popular. Such as JGorard's The Herball and R Dodonacus 1517-1585's Cruydboeck, are examples of this. Also, the same kind of work, when written in the author's native language, is more popular. When written in Latin, it goes against the norm of materia medica books and takes on the appearance of a botany book. For example, Tragus 1498-1554's "Kreuterbuce" (year edition) and "Stirpium maxim eaorum" (1652 edition) are two such books. There is also Kniphof's medicinal materia medica before Linnaeus, the so-called Offizinel Krauterbuch (1733-34 edition), etc., and Ferdinand Mull's Das grosse illustrierto Krauterbucb (first edition in 1860), which is still popular among the people today and is constantly being reprinted. It seems that Westerners implicitly regard ancient materia medica as a folk science and preserve it. Therefore, the authority of materia medica has not been diminished by the progress of botany, and it has the wonderful effect of complementing each other and developing together with botany. Finally, it was able to brew modern pharmacognosy (Pharmakognosie) (Materia medica). Who but the botanists and materia medica experts have bestowed a splendid and complete independent science from medicine and pharmacy for thousands of years? (End)

An Overview of Meningitis (3) 238

— Wang Xiaolan

(3) Spinal Tap Method: The patient's cerebrospinal cavity contains inflammatory exudate, and if the intracranial pressure increases, it will cause various stimulating symptoms. If the lumbar puncture method initiated by Dr. Oumche is performed to extract cerebrospinal fluid, the intracranial pressure will be reduced, and the symptoms will be alleviated accordingly. The amount of fluid extracted should be determined according to the level of intracranial pressure, usually about 20 to 80 cc each time, with an appropriate reduction for children, and it should be performed daily or every other day. If the cerebrospinal fluid is turbid and mixed with pus, sterile physiological saline can be injected during the puncture for repeated washing until it becomes clear, and then serum can be injected for even more remarkable results.

(4) Drug Therapy: If the patient has an excessively high fever or severe pain, antipyretic analgesics such as Aspirin, Phenacetin, and Cryogenine can be taken. If there is insomnia, delirium, or manic restlessness, sedatives and hypnotics such as potassium bromide, sodium bromide, and Veronal can be taken, or antispasmodic agents such as morphine and PantoponScopolamin can be injected, or green soap enemas can be used. If there is constipation or urinary retention, enemas or urinary catheterization can be performed, and laxatives such as calomel and rhubarb can be taken concurrently, or urinary disinfectants such as Urotropin can be taken. If there is heart failure, cardiotonics such as camphor products like Hexeton and digitalis products like Digalen can be used, either by injection or internal administration. Recently, for this disease, there are also those who use systemic disinfectants, such as Electrargol and Trypaflavin, by injection, and sometimes they are effective.

Prevention of Meningitis

When this disease is prevalent, attention should be paid to hygiene, maintaining cleanliness, and ensuring that houses have good air circulation and sufficient light. Carbolic acid or quicklime water should be sprinkled frequently in ditches, toilets, and dirty places for disinfection. Those who are fond of tobacco and alcohol, catch colds, are physically and mentally overworked, or have head injuries are all prone to developing this disease and should be especially careful to prevent it. Furthermore, people with lymphatic constitutions, or those who frequently have inflammation in the nose, throat, tonsils, etc., have a predisposing factor for this disease, and should regularly use disinfectant solutions, such as potassium chlorate water and hydrogen peroxide, to rinse their mouths and gargle their throats. If you feel dizzy, have a headache, or feel unwell, you should seek medical treatment at any time and do not ignore it.

Isolating patients and avoiding transmission are essential for prevention. Therefore, when this disease or suspected symptoms are found, they should be immediately separated from healthy people, and visits from relatives and friends should be prohibited. The patient's room and all sundries must not be used by others unless they have been disinfected. Places where many people gather inevitably have pathogens mixed in, so they must not be frequented. The mouth and nose are the gateways for germs to enter, so masks must be worn during the epidemic period of this disease, and they should be cleaned with disinfectant solutions from time to time. If talking to someone, do not get close. Anyone who enters the patient's home or is close to the patient should be injected with meningitis vaccine or meningitis serum.

Injecting meningitis vaccine into the human body can produce antibodies to resist germ invasion. Each person should be injected three times, with an interval of four to five days. The injection site can be subcutaneous or intramuscular in the thigh, and the dosage should be gradually increased, with a maximum limit of one cc. Appropriate reductions should be made for children. It is forbidden for those with elevated body temperature, beriberi, heart or kidney disease, or pregnancy. When the epidemic is rampant and rapid immunity is desired, ten cc of serum can be injected subcutaneously or intramuscularly, followed by the vaccine. Because the effect of serum is faster than that of the vaccine, but it is not as long-lasting as the vaccine, it is advisable to use both. Recently, the serum vaccine used is mostly produced by the Central Epidemic Prevention Office and the Shanghai Health Laboratory. It is particularly reliable to refer to the attached instructions before use. (End)

Farewell to Western Suit 239

— Song Guobin

Oh, Western suit! We are parting ways with you! I recall wearing you for more than ten years. In the beginning, I set sail ten thousand miles, carrying my books to Europe and the West. Without you for even a day, it was difficult to interact with the people of that country. I had no choice but to befriend you and adorn myself with you. After returning to my country, due to the habit that had been formed, I did not sever ties with you. Now, realizing the errors of my past blind following and lamenting the multitude of my countrymen who wear you, I extend the meaning of severing ties in the style of Ruan Ji and imitate Han Yu's "Farewell to Poverty," enumerating your crimes and rebuking you, saying:

Clothing is for fitting the body. If the body is not comfortable, what is the use of clothing? In ancient times, lofty hats and broad belts, wide sleeves and loose collars may have been incompatible with hygiene, but you have completely reversed this, valuing smallness above all else. Your collar is as stiff as a yoke, and your sleeves are as narrow as shackles. Every movement of the neck and every stretch of the thigh seems to be restricted by you. Nothing is more restrictive of freedom than you. This is your first crime.

Wearing linen in summer and fur in winter is a constant principle. You are only suitable for spring and autumn. Wearing you in summer, sweat sticks to the back. Wearing you in winter, snot and tears flow horizontally. Moreover, among all parts of the body, the chest is the weakest. You alone do not provide adequate protection here, causing body temperature to dissipate easily and cold air to easily invade, causing those who wear you to endure severe cold for your sake and develop diseases for your sake, harming hygiene more than anything else. This is your second crime.

Profits flow outward, and the country's resources are not strong. Rescuing the tide depends on advocating domestic goods. Your raw materials come from foreign lands, and your value is far higher than that of Chinese clothing. Patriots, though advocating domestic goods in word, wear foreign goods for your sake. Considering just you alone, the leakage of wealth each year is no less than hundreds of millions. The country is impoverished, and the people are exhausted. You are truly a sharp blade. This is your third crime.

You have three crimes and not a single virtue. Those who wear you are deluded by the new trends of Europe and America, forgetting their original appearance, using convenience as an excuse, and deceiving others with false beauty, thus forming an indissoluble bond with you! You also exploit the psychology of the ignorant masses, acting as a pioneer in destroying hygiene and a tool for economic aggression. If this is tolerable, what is not tolerable? If you speak of convenience, then what is wrong with Sun Yat-sen suits made in China? If you speak of beauty, then are not the flowing robes of China always the fair sons of a turbid age? Alas, if such people were to fill their minds with admiring the foreign, how many would not dye their beards yellow and their clothing blue? I now enumerate your crimes to proclaim them to my countrymen, not daring to consider myself enlightened, but also wishing to banish you from outside China and slightly recover our rights and interests, even by a fraction.

Using Chinese Medicine in Western Ways (Continued) 240

— Zhou Mengbai

(17) Galangal Galanga

Origin

This product is the rhizome of the Zingiberaceae plant Alpinia officinarum Hance, produced in the coastal provinces of Southeast China. It is collected in autumn and dried. Its original plant is a perennial herb with a round and straight stem, six to seven feet tall. The leaves are lanceolate, with short petioles, slightly fleshy. The flowers are irregular greenish-white. The fruit is a deep orange egg shape. Its seeds are called red cardamom.

Properties

This product is a cylindrical creeping rhizome with many fibrous roots. The outside is dark reddish-brown, with longitudinal wrinkles. Every five millimeters or so, there are light-colored, fire-tooth-shaped remnants of leaf sheaths. There are also many remnants of roots. The inside is reddish-brown, sometimes lighter than the outside, sometimes darker. It has a good and pungent odor and a spicy and very fragrant taste.

Composition

This product contains volatile oil. Its oil contains three kinds of crystals, namely, yellow flat crystals of Kampferid C16H12O6H2O, pale yellow prismatic crystals of Galangin, and granular crystals of Alpinin. It also contains resin, starch, and colloids.

Effect

This product is used as an aromatic stomachic. Its true ginger powder is yellowish-green and turns reddish-brown with sulfuric acid.

Appendix Old Sayings

It is pungent and hot, warms the stomach, disperses cold, promotes digestion, and relieves drunkenness. It treats cold pain in the stomach. The Yuanyang powder for treating coughs and hiccups contains galangal and licorice in equal parts, half an ounce each, and one mace of cloves, powdered. Take two mace per dose, infused in hot water.

(Note) The Japanese Kumatakeran is a different species of galangal. Mr. Tomitaro Makino determined its scientific name to be Alpinia Kunratake Makinoo. It is a mistake to regard it as galangal.
